    Municipal employees whose work schedule does not enable them time to vote during which time the polls are open shall be allowed up to one hour to vote. Such time shall be treated as regular work time for the purpose of pay and accrual of leaves. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.580 - Military leave. 
A.  Request for Military Leave of Absence. An employee who wishes to be granted military leave of absence must submit the request and a copy of his or her official orders or other records from the military service to his or her immediate supervisor or department head prior to the dates of attendance. If the reservist or National Guard member submits a copy of his or her official annual training schedule prior to beginning of the year's military activities, the employee need only submit separate requests and orders for those training duties not included on the annual schedule, or when the annual schedule is modified. 
B.  Active Duty. 
1.  An employee who enlists or is called into active duty for the military service of the United States or who, in time of national emergency, voluntarily enlists for active duty shall be granted military leave for the time necessary to permit completion of the military service. 
2.  In order to have re-employment rights, a person leaving active duty in the military service of the United States must apply to the municipality for re-employment within ninety (90) days after his or her separation from active duty, or within ninety (90) days after his or her release from hospitalization continuing after such separation for not more than one year. This applies to inductees and enlistees, as well as to reservists and National Guard members performing full active duty, as opposed to initial duty for training, or active or inactive duty training, or other active duty where different re-employment rights are defined by federal statute. 
C.  Reserve or National Guard Training Leave. 
1.  An employee who enlists as a reservist or a member of the National Guard shall be granted time off without pay for initial active duty for training, annual training encampment, weekend training drills, and other active and inactive training duty. 
2.  The reservist or National Guard member must report back to his or her civilian job at the beginning of his or her first regularly scheduled shift on the first day after the completion of initial active duty for training or other training duty plus the necessary travel time to return from the training site to the place of employment. He or she is also entitled to a reasonable rest time, and a reasonable time thereafter if return is delayed by factors beyond his or her control. If an employee fails to report to his or her job within this specified time period, he or she may be subject to the penalties which would be imposed on any employee who is tardy or absent without permission. 
3.  If an employee separates his or her employment with the municipality in order to enlist in the Reserves or National Guard, he or she must reapply to the municipality within thirty-one (31) days after his or her separation from initial active duty for training in the Reserves or National Guard in order to retain re-employment rights. 
D.  Federal Statute. An employee who participates in any branch of the military service of the United States is covered by and subject to federal statute, United States Code Title 38, Chapter 43, and all other applicable statutes. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.590 - Funeral leave. 
    All regularly scheduled full-time employees are eligible for funeral leave with pay. Time off with pay will be granted according to the following: 
A.  In the event of death of a member of the immediate family. (Immediate family is defined as an employee's spouse, parents, step-parents, children, step-children, brothers, sisters, step-brothers, step-sisters, grandparents, grandchildren and great grandchildren. The term also includes a spouse's equivalent of the above.) Not to exceed five days; 
B.  In the event of death of an aunt, uncle, nephew or niece, or spouse equivalent. Not to exceed one day. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.600 - Holidays. 
A.  The municipality of Sisseton recognizes and observes the following as paid holidays for eligible employees: 
New Year's Day January 1 Martin Luther King Jr. Day 3rd Monday in January Presidents' Day 3rd Monday in February Memorial Day Last Monday in May Independence Day July 4 Labor Day 1st Monday in September Native Americans' Day 2nd Monday in October Veterans' Day November 11 Thanksgiving Day 4th Thursday in November Christmas Day December 25  
and all other days proclaimed by the mayor. 
B.  When a holiday falls on a Saturday, the preceding Friday is observed as the paid holiday for eligible municipal employees. If a holiday falls on a Sunday, it is observed on the following Monday. 
C.  Employees ineligible for paid holiday leave will be granted a day off without pay in observance of a holiday. 
D.  Work on a Holiday. 
1.  An employee required to work on a paid holiday observed by the municipality will receive regular pay for those hours worked in addition to holiday pay. 
2.  A liquor store clerk who works on a part-time basis and is not eligible for holiday pay will receive double time for hours worked on a holiday. 
3.  A Police Department employee required to work on a paid holiday observed by the municipality will receive regular pay for hours worked and have the option to be granted an additional eight (8) hours to be added on to their vacation leave or paid an additional eight (8) hours of holiday pay. 
E.  Paid Holiday on Regular Day Off. If a paid holiday recognized by the municipality falls on an employee's regularly scheduled day off, the employee will be granted an additional eight hours to be added on to his or her vacation leave. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
(Ord. No. 647, 12-28-2017) 
Article 8. - Separation from Municipal Service 

2.24.610 - General policies. 
A.  Definitions. 
    "Involuntary separation" means layoff or discharge. Involuntary separation is not initiated by the employee. 
    "Voluntary separation" means written resignation, extended absence without proper notification, or retirement. Voluntary separation is initiated by the employee. 
B.  Return of Municipal Property. Municipal employees are expected to return all municipal property at the time of their departure from municipal service. The municipality reserves the right to withhold from the employee's final paycheck the amount for any property that is not returned or for which there is no explanation for the absence of the property. The municipality may take further action if necessary to recover municipal property. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.620 - Voluntary separation. 
A.  Resignation. A municipal employee may resign from municipal service by giving his or her appointing authority written notice of his or her resignation at least two weeks in advance of his or her leaving municipal service. In extenuating circumstances, the mayor may accept the employee's resignation as taking effect immediately. 
B.  Unnotified Absence. If an employee is absent for more than three consecutive days without proper notification in accordance with the attendance policy, he or she shall be considered to have voluntarily resigned his or her position in municipal service. Reinstatement upon presentation of extenuating circumstances or reason for such absence shall be at the discretion of the mayor. Any unnotified absence of less than three days may result in disciplinary action. 
C.  Retirement Age. There is no mandatory retirement age for municipal employees. However, all employees must continue to meet the performance requirements for their position. 
D.  South Dakota Retirement System. The municipality of Sisseton is a member of the South Dakota Retirement System (SDRS) and follows the retirement system law as set forth in SDCL 3-12. All eligible employees (see Article 3 and Section 2.24.470(C)) will be members of the SDRS and all benefits will be administered through the SDRS office in Pierre. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.630 - Involuntary separation. 
A.  Discharge Disciplinary Interview. In cases of discharge the employee will be granted full due process rights as set forth in Section 2.24.670(H). 
B.  Unemployment Compensation. The municipality follows the state of South Dakota unemployment laws as found in SDCL Title 61. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.640 - Exit interviews. 
A.  It is a policy of the municipality of Sisseton, for the finance officer to conduct an exit interview prior to an employee's separation from municipal employment. The exit interview is conducted for several purposes, including: (1) to resolve all outstanding matters between the municipality and the employee, (2) to advise the employee of the effect his or her separation will have upon all benefits and what benefits he or she has coming upon separation, and (3) to aid the municipality in gathering information to help improve the municipality's working environment and other employment relationships. 
B.  At the time of the exit interview, employees are expected to return all municipal property as specified in Section 2.24.610(B). 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.650 - Misconduct defined. 
    The following is a partial listing of employee misconduct that may result in disciplinary action up to and including immediate discharge. This list is not intended to completely list all employee misconduct that may result in the above, but rather is provided as a guideline by which employees can judge actions that will not be tolerated by the municipality. 
A.  Incompetent, inefficient, unreliable, unwilling, or incapable of fulfilling his or her job duties as assigned; 
B.  Inadequate performance of duties; 
C.  Neglect of duty; 
D.  Insubordination; 
E.  Conviction of a felony or misdemeanor offense which might adversely reflect on or create doubt about the moral character, credibility or reliability of the employee; 
F.  Theft or misappropriation of municipal property; 
G.  Failure to observe drug and alcohol policies of the municipality; 
H.  Failure to observe harassment policies of the municipality; 
I.  Knowing or wilful violation of municipal ordinances; 
J.  Unauthorized absences; 
K.  Habitual tardiness; 
L.  Abuse of sick leave; 
M.  Sleeping/loafing during working hours; 
N.  Drinking, gambling, fighting, swearing, and similar unprofessional activities, while on the job; 
O.  Sexual harassment, acting in a way that could be construed as such, for example, by using inappropriate language, keeping or posting inappropriate materials on his or her computer; 
P.  Engaging in false recordkeeping or communication of any kind, including false expense, attendance, financial or similar reports and statements; 
Q.  Disclosure of confidential information; 
R.  Offensive or inconsiderate conduct, or use of abusive language in public, or toward the public, municipal officials, or fellow employees while on duty; 
S.  Personal acceptance or appropriation of any fee, gift, tip or other gratuity or remuneration received solely for the performance of official duties in connection with municipal employment; 
T.  Knowing, intentional or repeated falsification of any application for employment or any municipal record, report or time sheet; 
U.  Wilful alteration, destruction or waste of municipal property, facilities, equipment or records; 
V.  Serious or repeated disorderly conduct or horseplay; 
W.  Threatening, intimidating, coercing or interfering with supervisors or other employees; 
X.  Deliberate attempts to injure another employee or fighting on municipal property while on the job; 
Y.  Unauthorized possession of firearms, explosives or any dangerous weapons while performing municipal work; 
Z.  Recklessness resulting in a serious accident while on duty, whether on or off municipal property. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.660 - Misconduct. 
    Employee misconduct will not be tolerated and may result in immediate disciplinary action. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
Article 9. - Disciplinary Action and Grievance Procedure 

2.24.670 - Disciplinary action. 
    Disciplinary actions shall be applied when the city council determines such actions are necessary. A disciplinary action may be in the form of oral reprimand, written reprimand, suspension, demotion or reassignment, or dismissal as defined below. The municipality may, but is not required to, apply these actions progressively: 
A.  Oral Reprimand. The mayor, council president or department head may orally reprimand an employee. This informal disciplinary consultation may be documented on an employee's performance appraisal or referenced in further progressive disciplinary actions. 
B.  Written Reprimand. The mayor, council president or department head may discipline an employee by written reprimand. 
C.  Suspension Without Pay. The mayor, council president or department head with approval of the city council may temporarily suspend an employee without pay for disciplinary purposes. Suspension shall be for no more than ten (10) working days. 
D.  Demotion or Reassignment. The mayor, council president or department head with the approval of the city council may reduce an employee's salary, assign the employee to a lower position, or change the employee's duties within his or her current position or use any combination of the above for disciplinary purposes. 
E.  Dismissal. The mayor, council president or department head with the approval of the city council may terminate an employee from municipal employment for disciplinary purposes. 
F.  Voluntary Separations and Grievances. Employees who voluntarily terminate their employment will have their grievances immediately dismissed. 
G.  Non-grievable Actions. Oral and written reprimands and terminations of employees during their employee-in-training period are not grievable except on the basis of a prohibited form of discrimination. 
H.  Disciplinary Interview. Before formal disciplinary actions are taken (suspension without pay, demotion, or dismissal), the mayor, council president or department head shall: 
1.  Notify the employee in writing of the proposed disciplinary action. The notice shall state the reason(s) for the action, including any prior disciplinary actions and the facts of any other incidents upon which the present disciplinary action is based; 
2.  Hold a disciplinary interview to give the employee an opportunity to present reasons, orally or in writing, why the action should not be taken; 
3.  Inform the employee in writing of the final decision, effective date of the disciplinary action, and his or her right to appeal such decision to the city council, as followed in Section 2.24.680(D), by filing a written notice of disagreement with the mayor or council president, within five working days of receiving the response. If the employee fails to appeal the decision within five working days the action shall become final. 
I.  Signing Requirements. 
1.  In all cases of formal disciplinary action the employee will be required to sign the written notice of discipline and such notice shall be dated and placed in the employee's permanent personnel file. If the employee refuses to sign the notice, a notation to that effect shall be made by the mayor, council president or department head with another city employee or official as a witness. The employee may submit a written statement of response to the disciplinary action which shall be attached to and remain with the disciplinary action in his or her permanent personnel file. Documentation of such discipline may be submitted to the mayor for review. 
2.  In all instances in this policy where an employee is required to sign, signing does not imply agreement with the action, only that the contents have been made known to or discussed with the employee. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.680 - Grievance procedure. 
A.  Purpose. The purpose of this grievance procedure is to provide a just and equitable method for the resolution of grievances without discrimination, coercion, restraint, or reprisal against any employee or group of employees who may submit to or be involved in a grievance. 
B.  Definition of a Grievance. A grievance is a complaint by an employee or a group of employees concerning the interpretation or application of the provisions of rules or regulations governing conditions of employment, personnel practices and procedures, or conditions which have not been resolved satisfactorily in an informal manner between the employee(s) and the city council. 
C.  Employee Notice of Disagreement. 
1.  If the employee disagrees with any action of the city council, he or she may within ten (10) working days (working days does not mean calendar days) from the date on which the employee became aware of the action or should have reasonably been aware of the action, submit to the city council a written notice of disagreement stating the reasons for disagreement and the action that he or she desires. 
2.  If the employee disagrees with the response to the grievance or the city council fails to respond to the grievance within five working days, the employee may file a written notice of disagreement with the mayor within five working days of receiving the response. If the employee fails to appeal the decision within five working days, the grievance shall be considered waived. 
D.  Appearance Before the City Council. At the next meeting (or a special meeting) of the city council following the employee's notice of disagreement, the grievant employee may appear before the city council in open or executive session to discuss his or her grievance. After the employee's appearance before the city council, the mayor or council president shall, in writing, furnish the decision of the city council to the grievant employee. If the grievant employee fails to appear before the city council on his or her scheduled date of hearing, he or she shall be deemed to have waived any disagreement with the decisionmaking authority decision and shall waive all rights to grieve such decision. 
E.  Appeal from the Decision of the City Council. If the grievant employee disagrees with the written decision of the city council as provided by the mayor, he or she may within thirty (30) calendar days (calendar days does not mean working days) after receipt of the decision, initiate an appeal to the State Department of Labor in accordance with the provisions of SDCL 3-18-15.2. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
Article 10. - Drug and Alcohol Abuse Policy 

2.24.690 - Municipality's commitment to drug and alcohol free workplace. 
A.  The municipality of Sisseton has a strong commitment to its employees to provide a safe, healthful, and productive work environment and to promote high standards of employee health. Consistent with the spirit and intent of this objective, the municipality will act to eliminate any substance abuse which could impair an employee's ability to safely and effectively perform a particular job and which increases the potential for accidents, absenteeism, substandard performance, and tends to undermine public confidence in the municipality's work force. The municipality's goals are to establish and maintain a work environment that is free from the effects of alcohol and drug abuse and to maintain the reputation and integrity of the municipality of Sisseton by preventing unacceptable behavior by its employees that discredits the municipality of Sisseton and its employees. 
B.  While the municipality has no intention of unreasonably intruding into the private lives of its employees, the municipality does expect employees to report for work in a condition to perform their duties, make the work environment safe for other employees, and represent a proper image to the citizens. It is clear that employee off-the-job, as well as on-the-job, involvement with drugs and alcohol can have an impact on the municipality's goals. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.700 - Drug and alcohol abuse policies. 
    Following are the policies of the municipality regarding drug and alcohol abuse: 
A.  The unlawful manufacture, distribution, dispensing, possession or use of controlled drugs or substances, or the use of alcohol while on duty, on or off business property owned or leased by the municipality is proper cause for disciplinary action. 
B.  Any illegal controlled drug or substance possessed while on duty by employees will be turned over to the appropriate criminal justice agencies and may result in criminal prosecution. This does not apply to public safety officers who are in possession of an illegal controlled drug or substance while acting in the line of duty. 
C.  It is not permitted for an employee to be under the influence of controlled drugs or substances or alcohol on the job, except as provided for in subsection D of this section. 
D.  The legal use of controlled drugs or substances prescribed by a licensed physician is not prohibited, but employees in positions where side effects of the prescribed medication could affect performance and safety on the job are required to make such use known to their supervisor. 
E.  The illegal use, sale, and possession of controlled drugs or substances while off duty and off municipal premises which results in a criminal conviction is unacceptable. Off-duty, alcohol-related, criminal convictions are also unacceptable. They may affect the job performance and the confidence of the public in the municipality's ability to meet its responsibilities. Such off-the-job conduct may be proper cause for disciplinary action. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.710 - Testing for drugs or alcohol. 
A.  The municipality may request that the employee undergo drug and alcohol testing if there is a "reasonable suspicion" that the employee is under the influence of drugs or alcohol during work hours. "Reasonable suspicion" means an articulable belief based on specific facts and reasonable inferences drawn from those facts that an employee is under the influence of drugs or alcohol. Circumstances which constitute a basis for determining reasonable suspicion may include, but are not limited to: 
1.  A pattern of abnormal or erratic behavior which is so unusual that it warrants summoning a supervisor, department head or other individual for assistance; 
2.  Information provided by a reliable and credible source with personal knowledge; 
3.  Direct observation of drug or alcohol use; 
4.  Presence of the physical symptoms of drug or alcohol use; (i.e., glossy or bloodshot eyes, alcohol odor on breath, slurred speech, poor coordination and/or reflexes); 
5.  Possession of substances in violation of the municipality's drug and alcohol policy. 
B.  The employee, where "reasonable suspicion" exists, may be asked to submit to blood and urine testing by a qualified medical physician or hospital at the municipality's expense. Prior to testing, the proper authority shall secure a signed release statement from the employee to have the hospital/physician release medical information to the municipality (see appendix five). 
C.  An employee who refuses to consent to a drug and alcohol test when reasonable suspicion exists may be subject to disciplinary action. 
D.  A positive result from the drug and/or alcohol test confirming the reasonable suspicion may result in disciplinary action. 
E.  The proper authority is required to detail in writing the specific facts, symptoms, or observations which led to the reasonable suspicion. This documentation shall be given to the finance officer and placed in the employee's personnel file only if confirmed by the drug and/or alcohol test (see appendix five). 
F.  All information from an employee's drug and/or alcohol test is confidential, and only those with a need to know are to be informed of the results. Disclosure of test results to any other person, agency, or organization is prohibited unless written authorization is obtained from the employee. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.720 - Drugs to be tested for. 
    The following drug groups were selected based on the ability of each drug to adversely affect physical/mental performance. All are controlled substances under state and federal law. 
A.  Alcohol, ethyl; 
B.  Amphetamines/methamphetamines (i.e., speed); 
C.  Barbiturates (i.e., to include but not limited to amobarbital, butabarbital, phenobarbital, cecobarbital); 
D.  Cocaine, cocaine metabolites; 
E.  Benzodiazepines; 
F.  Opiates (i.e., to include but not limited to codeine, heroin, morphine, hydromorphone, hyrocodone); 
G.  Phencyclidine (PCP); 
H.  THC (Marijuana) metabolite. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.730 - Employee responsibilities. 
A.  An employee must not report to work while his or her ability to perform his or her job duties is impaired due to on or off duty alcohol or drug use. Employees called in for emergency duty to work outside their regular work schedule must not report to work impaired by off-duty alcohol or drug use. 
B.  An employee must not possess or use alcohol or illegal drugs or prescription drugs without a prescription during working hours or while subject to duty, on breaks, or during meal periods. 
C.  An employee must notify his or her supervisor, before beginning work, when taking any medication or drugs, prescription or non-prescription, which may interfere with the safe and effective performance of duties or operation of municipal equipment. 
D.  An employee must notify his or her immediate supervisor of any drug or alcohol related criminal statute conviction for a violation occurring in the workplace no later than five days after such conviction. Any violations of the above stated policy may result in immediate disciplinary action. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.740 - Management responsibilities and guidelines. 
A.  Supervisors and department heads shall not physically search the persons of employees nor shall they search the personal possessions of employees without the freely given consent of, and in the presence of, the employee. 
B.  Supervisors and department heads shall notify the appropriate law enforcement agency when they have reasonable suspicion to believe that an employee may have illegal drugs in his or her possession or in an area jointly or fully controlled by the municipality. 
C.  Any supervisor or department head encountering an employee who refuses to consent to a drug and/or alcohol analysis when "reasonable suspicion" has been identified, shall remind the employee of the requirements of the policy and that he or she may be subject to disciplinary action. The reason(s) for the refusal shall be considered in determining the appropriate disciplinary action. Where there is reasonable suspicion that the employee is under the influence of alcohol or drugs, the manager or supervisor should direct the employee to remain at work for a reasonable time until the employee can be safely transported home. 
D.  Nothing in this policy shall be interpreted as constituting any waiver of or limitation on the municipality's responsibility to maintain discipline, or the right to invoke disciplinary measures, nor the employee's right to due process and the processing of grievances concerning such disciplinary measures in accordance with the grievance procedure set forth in Article 9. 
E.  Whenever disciplinary action is used in this policy, it shall include but not be limited to: oral reprimand, written reprimand, suspension, demotion or discharge. 
F.  Each employee will be given a copy of the municipality's policy on drug and alcohol substance abuse. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
Article 11. - Americans with Disabilities Act 

2.24.750 - Grievance procedure. 
A.  The Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA) provides comprehensive civil rights protection to individuals with disabilities in the areas of employment, public accommodations, state and local government services and programs, and telecommunications. Title II of the ADA states, in part, that "no otherwise qualified disabled individual shall, solely by reason of such disability, be excluded from the participation in, be denied the benefits of, or be subject to discrimination" in programs or activities sponsored by a public entity. 
B.  The municipality of Sisseton has adopted this grievance procedure to provide prompt and equitable resolution of complaints alleging any action prohibited by the U.S. Department of Justice regulations implementing Title II of the ADA. 
C.  Any individual who believes that he or she or a specific class of individuals with disabilities has been subjected to unlawful discrimination on the basis of that disability by Sisseton may, by himself or herself or by any authorized representative, file a complaint. 
D.  Complaints should be addressed to: Sisseton City Council, 513 Veterans Avenue, Sisseton, SD 57262 (605)698-3391. 
1.  A complaint must be filed in writing and contain: the name and address of the individual or representative filing the complaint, a description of the alleged discriminatory action in sufficient detail to inform the entity of the nature and date of the alleged violation, and be signed by the complainant or authorized representative. Complaints filed on behalf of third parties must describe or identify the alleged victims of the discrimination. 
2.  The complaint must be filed within one hundred eighty (180) days after the alleged violation occurs. This time may be extended for good cause shown. 
3.  The city council shall promptly conduct an informal, but thorough, investigation of the complaint. All interested parties shall be afforded an opportunity to submit evidence relevant to the complaint. 
4.  A written determination of the validity of the complaint and a description of the resolution shall be issued and a copy forwarded to the complainant no later than ten (10) days after completion of this investigation. The finding shall include: findings of fact and conclusions of law, a description of a remedy for any violation found, and a notice of the rights available to both the entity and the complainant, including the complainant's right to file a private suit. 
5.  Files and records of all complaints filed shall be maintained. 
6.  The complainant may request a reconsideration of the complaint in cases where he or she is dissatisfied with the resolution. The request for reconsideration must be made to Sisseton City Council within ten (10) days of the original finding. 
7.  Nothing in this grievance procedure shall be construed as preventing an individual from pursuit of other remedies including filing the complaint with any federal agency he or she believes is appropriate or with the U.S. Department of Justice. This procedure also does not preclude the individual's right to file a lawsuit in federal district court. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
Article 12. - Appointive Officials 

2.24.760 - Definition. 
    An appointive official is an individual who holds a position in a municipality as specified in SDCL 9-14-1 (see Section 2.24.770). 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.770 - Appointive officials to be appointed. 
A.  First Class Municipality. The appointive officers in a first class municipality are the finance officer (auditor, treasurer), attorney, engineer, chief of police and such other officers as provided in municipal ordinance. 
B.  Second and Third Class Municipalities. The appointive officers in second and third class municipalities are the finance officer (auditor, treasurer) and other such officers as provided by municipal ordinance. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.780 - Appointment of appointive officials. 
A.  Aldermanic. The mayor appoints all municipal officials with the approval of the common council. 
B.  Commissioner and Trustee. Appointment of municipal officials are made by a majority vote of the members elected to the governing board. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
2.24.790 - Applicable policies to municipal officials. 
    The following articles of this chapter shall apply to municipal officials: 
    Article 1: All sections; 
    Article 2: All sections; 
    Article 3: All sections; 
    Article 4: Not applicable; 
    Article 5: Applicable if you determine such officials are covered by FLSA; 
    Article 6: All sections; 
    Article 7: All sections; 
    Article 8: Not applicable; 
    Article 9: Not applicable; 
    Article 10: All sections; 
    Article 11: All sections. 
(Ord. 571 (part), 2005) 
Title 3 - REVENUE AND FINANCE 
Chapter 3.04 - FISCAL PROVISIONS GENERALLY 

3.04.010 - Salaries. 
    The salaries of the various officers shall be paid from such funds as may be from time to time designated by resolution of the city council. 
(Prior code § 1-3-1) 
3.04.020 - Waterworks revenues. 
    All revenues of the city received from the operation of the city waterworks shall be paid into the city treasury and shall be credited to the water fund of the city. 
(Prior code § 1-3-2) 
3.04.030 - Liquor revenues. 
    All revenues of the city received from the operation of the city liquor store shall be paid into the city treasury and shall be credited to the liquor fund of the city. Revenues from approved licenses for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be credited to the general fund. 
(Prior code § 1-3-3) 
3.04.040 - Service revenues. 
    All revenues of the city received from the operation of the parks, airport, sewer service, and garbage collection shall be paid into the city treasury and shall be credited to such special funds as may be designated by resolution of the city council. 
(Prior code § 1-3-4) 
3.04.050 - Miscellaneous revenues. 
    All revenues of the city received from licenses, fines, and other fees shall be paid into the city treasury and credited to the general fund unless otherwise specifically provided by ordinance. 
(Prior code § 1-3-5) 
Chapter 3.08 - PROPERTY TAXES 

3.08.010 - Established. 
    Pursuant to Article XI, Section 2 of the South Dakota Constitution and SDCL 9-21A, it is hereby the intention of the city to create two classes of property, urban and rural, for the purposes of ad valorem property taxation within the city. 
(Ord. 553 § 1, 2002: Ord. 346 § 1, 1977) 
3.08.020 - Definitions. 
A.  "Urban property" is all platted property developed for commercial, industrial or urban residential purposes within the corporate limits of the municipalities of the city. 
B.  "Rural property" is all property platted or unplatted property not developed for commercial, industrial or urban residential purposes within the commercial limits of the city. 
(Ord. 553 § 2, 2002: Ord. 346 § 2, 1977) 
3.08.030 - Exemptions. 
    This chapter shall not apply to taxes levied for the payment of bonds. 
(Ord. 553 § 3, 2002: Ord. 346 § 3, 1977) 
3.08.040 - Rural classification. 
    The rural class of property includes only such platted or unplatted lands as in the judgment of the city council are rural in nature, are used or usable for agriculture and are not developed for commercial, industrial or urban residential purposes as the aforementioned reasons are not benefited to the same degree as other land by municipal services financed by general taxation. 
(Ord. 553 § 4, 2002: Ord. 346 § 4, 1977) 
3.08.050 - Urban classification. 
    The urban property includes all lands within the municipality not included in the rural service district. 
(Ord. 553 § 5, 2002: Ord. 346 § 5, 1977) 
3.08.060 - Rural classification-Application. 
    An individual may apply in writing to the city council of the city for a rural classification. For a tract of land to be included in the rural property classification, it must have the approval of a majority of the members of the city council. 
(Ord. 553 § 6, 2002: Ord. 346 § 6, 1977) 
3.08.070 - Mill levy and assessed value. 
    The mill levy and assessed value on the rural land classification annexed or contained within the municipal boundaries of the city shall not exceed the average mill levy and average assessed value on the unannexed agriculture land in adjoining townships in the county as long as the land within the municipal boundaries or that is annexed remains in the rural property designation. 
(Ord. 553 § 7, 2002: Ord. 346 § 7, 1977) 
3.08.080 - Discretionary tax formula. 
A.  Residential Structures. Any new residential structure, or any addition to or renovation of an existing structure, located within a redevelopment neighborhood, which new structure, addition, or renovation has a true and full vale of five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) or more, added to real property shall qualify to be assessed pursuant to the discretionary formula described in subsection B. In order to improve the quality of housing, all real property located within the city limits of Sisseton, South Dakota shall qualify as property located in a redevelopment neighborhood. The redevelopment neighborhood is being established because the area includes buildings or improvements which by reason of age, deterioration, obsolescence, and dilapidation injuriously affect the area to the detriment of public health, safety, morals or welfare and because the development of housing is being prevented by the predominance of defective or inadequate street layout, faulty lot layout in relation to size, adequacy, accessibility, or usefulness, the deterioration of site improvements, and obsolete platting. 
B.  Discretionary Formula. Any real property qualifying for the discretionary formula pursuant to this chapter shall be assessed in accordance with SDCL 10-6-55 with the following reductions in place for the qualifying property: 
First Year 20%; 
Second Year 40%; 
Third Year 60%; 
Fourth Year 80%; and 
Fifth Year 100%. 
(Ord. No. 620, 7-8-2013) 
Chapter 3.12 - SALES AND USE TAX 

3.12.010 - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this chapter is to provide additional needed revenue for the municipality of Sisseton, Roberts County, South Dakota, by imposing a municipal retail sales and use tax pursuant to the powers granted to the municipality by the State of South Dakota, by SDCL 10-52 entitled: Uniform Municipal Non-Ad Valorem Tax Law, and Acts amendatory thereto. 
(Ord. 561 § 1, 2003; Ord. 559 § 1, 2003; Ord. 500 § 1, 1997) 
3.12.020 - Effective date and enactment of tax. 
    From and after the first day of January, 2006, there is imposed as a municipal retail occupational sales and service tax upon the privilege of engaging in business a tax measured by two percent on the gross receipts of all persons engaged in business within the jurisdiction of the municipality of Sisseton, Roberts County, South Dakota, who are subject to the South Dakota Retail Occupational Sales and Service Tax Act, SDCL 10-45 and Acts amendatory. 
(Ord. 574, 2005: Ord. 561 § 2, 2003; Ord. 559 § 2, 2003; Ord. 500 § 2, 1997) 
3.12.030 - Use tax. 
    In addition, there is imposed an excise tax on the privilege of use, storage and consumption within the jurisdiction of the municipality of tangible personal property or services purchased from and after the first of January, 2004, at the same rate as the municipal sales and service tax upon all transactions or use, storage and consumption which are subject to the South Dakota Use Tax Act SDCL 10-46, and Acts amendatory thereto. 
(Ord. 561 § 3, 2003; Ord. 559 § 3, 2003; Ord. 500 § 5, 1997) 
3.12.040 - Collection. 
    Such tax is levied pursuant to authorization granted by SDCL 10-52, and Acts amendatory thereto, and shall be collected by the South Dakota Department of Revenue and Regulation in accordance with the same rules and regulations applicable to the state sales tax and under such additional rules and regulations as the secretary of revenue and regulation of the State of South Dakota shall lawfully prescribe. 
(Ord. 561 § 4, 2003; Ord. 559 § 4, 2003; Ord. 500 § 6, 1997) 
3.12.050 - Interpretation. 
    It is declared to be the intention of this chapter and the taxes levied hereunder that the same shall be interpreted and construed in the same manner as all sections of the South Dakota Retail Occupational Sales and Service Tax Act, SDCL 10-45 and Acts amendatory thereto, and the South Dakota Use Tax, SDCL 10-46 and Acts amendatory thereto, and that this is considered a similar tax except for the rate thereof to that tax. 
(Ord. 561 § 5, 2003; Ord. 559 § 5, 2003; Ord. 500 § 7, 1997) 
3.12.060 - Penalty. 
    Any person failing or refusing to make reports or payments prescribed by this chapter and the rules and regulations relating to the ascertainment and collection of the tax herein levied shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or imprisoned in the county jail for thirty (30) days or both such fine and imprisonment. In addition, all such collection remedies authorized by SDCL 10-45, and Acts amendatory thereto, and SDCL 10-46, and Acts amendatory thereto are authorized for the collection of these excise taxes by the department of revenue and regulation. 
(Ord. 561 § 6, 2003; Ord. 559 § 6, 2003; Ord. 500 § 9, 1997) 
3.12.070 - Municipal gross receipts tax. 
A.  Purpose. The purpose of this ordinance is to provide additional needed revenue for the Municipality of Sisseton, Roberts County, South Dakota, by imposing a municipal gross receipts tax pursuant to the powers granted to the municipality by the State of South Dakota, by SDCL 10-52A, and Acts amendatory thereto. 
B.  Effective Date and Enactment of Tax. From and after the first day of July, 2016, there is hereby imposed a municipal gross receipts tax of one percent (1%) upon the gross receipts from the sale of leases or rentals of hotel, motel, campsites or other lodging accommodations within the municipality for periods of less than twenty-eight (28) consecutive days, the sale of alcoholic beverages as defined in SDCL 35-1-1, and establishments where the public is invited to eat, dine or purchase and carry out prepared food for immediate consumption. The tax applies to the gross receipts of all persons engaged in business within the jurisdiction of the Municipality of Sisseton, Roberts County, South Dakota, who are subject to the South Dakota Retail Occupational Sales and Service Tax, SDCL 10-45 and Acts amendatory thereto. 
C.  Collection. Such tax is levied pursuant to authorization granted by SDCL 10-52A and Acts amendatory thereto, and shall be collected by the South Dakota Department of Revenue and Regulation in accordance with the same rules and regulations applicable to the state sales tax and under such additional rules and regulations as the Secretary of Revenue of the State of South Dakota shall lawfully prescribe. 
D.  Interpretation. It is declared to be the intention of this ordinance and the taxes levied hereunder that the same shall be interpreted and construed in the same manner as all sections of the South Dakota Retail Occupational Sales and Service Act, SDCL 10-45 and Acts amendatory thereto, and that this shall be considered a similar tax except for the rate thereof to that tax. 
E.  Use of Revenue. Any revenues received under this ordinance may be used only for the purpose of land acquisition, architectural fees, construction costs, payment for civic center auditoriums or athletic facility buildings, including the maintenance, staffing and operations of such facilities, and the promotion and advertising of the municipality, its facilities, attractions and activities. 
F.  Penalty. Any person failing or refusing to make reports or payments prescribed by this ordinance and the rules and regulations relating to the ascertainment and collection of the tax herein levied shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or imprisoned in the municipal jail for thirty (30) days or both such fine and imprisonment. In addition, all such collection remedies authorized by SDCL 10-45, and Acts amendatory thereto, are hereby authorized for the collection of these excise taxes by the Department of Revenue. 
(Ord. No. 609, §§ 1-6, 2-28-2011; Ord. No. 637, 2-8-2016) 
Title 5 - BUSINESS LICENSES AND REGULATIONS 
Chapter 5.04 - BUSINESS LICENSES GENERALLY 
Sections: 

5.04.010 - Licenses-Generally. 
A.  Every person, firm, or corporation engaging in a trade, business or occupation as follows: pawnbroker, dealer in second hand goods, dealer in items designed for use with illegal drugs or cannabis, junkyards, alcoholic beverage dealers, within the city shall obtain a business license from the city. 
B.  Dogs, cats and bicycles must also be licensed if they are to be kept within the city. 
(Ord. 531, 2002) 
Chapter 5.08 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Sections: 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 617, §§ I-VII, adopted Dec. 10, 2012, repealed former Ch. 5.08, §§ 5.08.010-5.08.070, and enacted a new Ch. 5.08 as set out herein. Former Ch. 5.08 pertained to the same subject matter and derived from Ord. No. 527, § § 1-7, adopted in 2002 and Ord. No. 599, adopted May 11, 2009. 

5.08.010 - Permit. 
    No person or persons shall within the limits of the city of Sisseton, vend, give away or deliver any intoxicating liquors or malt beverages without first having obtained a permit from the City Council of the City of Sisseton to do so. Provided, however, that the provisions of this section shall not apply to a registered pharmacist in selling such liquors in compliance with the Laws of the State of South Dakota relating to the registered pharmacists selling the same under permit. It shall be unlawful for any person or persons within the city of Sisseton to engage in the business of selling or offering for sale any intoxicating liquors or malt beverages without first having procured a license therefore from the City Council of the City of Sisseton. 
(Ord. No. 617, § I, 12-10-2012) 
5.08.020 - Operating agreements-Mark up on alcoholic beverage. 
A.  Liquor Licenses. All on sale liquor licensees within the City of Sisseton shall be required to enter into operating agreements with the City of Sisseton, and shall be required thereunder to purchase all alcoholic beverages sold in such establishments through the package liquor store owned by the City of Sisseton at a price of ten (10) percent over the wholesale price of said alcoholic beverages to the city, exclusive of freight charges. 
B.  Malt Beverage Licenses. All malt beverages sold within the City of Sisseton, whether through on-sale or off-sale licenses shall be purchased through the package liquor store owned by the City of Sisseton and all such malt beverages shall be marked up ten (10) percent as they are under the existing operating agreements with the on-sale liquor licensees. All liquor and malt beverage licensees will act in accordance with South Dakota Codified Laws as amended and any local regulations. 
C.  Authority to Close Establishment Failing to Make Report and/or Pay Ten (10) percent Mark-Up in a Timely Manner. 
1.  The ten (10) percent mark-up on all liquor and malt beverages sold by on-sale or off-sale licensees within the City of Sisseton shall be due and payable no later than the 10th day of the month following purchase. A monthly report on the form prescribed and furnished by the City of Sisseton shall be filed with the City Finance Officer at the office at the City Hall no later than 12:00 o'clock noon on the 10th day of each month. 
2.  This report shall show gross sales for the preceding month of liquor and/or malt beverages and a calculation of the ten (10) percent mark-up due to the city and shall be sworn to by the owner or manager of the establishment and said report shall be accompanied by a check for the full amount due the city. 
3.  Failure to report and/or pay the ten (10) percent mark-up, or selling or having on the premises of a licensed establishment, beverages procured from sources other than the municipal liquor store shall constitute a violation of this ordinance. 
4.  In addition to criminal penalties as hereinafter provided, any licensee who fails to report and/or pay the ten (10) percent mark-up, as set forth above shall be closed for business until said report is filed and said payment is made. 
a.  If a licensee fails to file a report or pay the ten (10) percent mark-up as provided above, the city council shall issue an order to show cause to said licensee citing him to appear before the city council at a time and place to be set forth in said order, no less than five days after service of said notice on said licensee. 
b.  At that hearing, the licensee shall be required to show cause why he has not filed the monthly report and/or paid the ten (10) percent mark-up for the month to the city. 
c.  Unless the report is filed and mark-up paid in full before the date and time set for said hearing, or unless the licensee shows good cause at said hearing for his failure to make the report and pay the mark-up, the city shall enter an order to the Chief of Police or any other law enforcement officer in the county to close said business until such time as said report has been filed and said mark-up is paid in full. 
D.  Conditions. As a condition of being granted a liquor license and/or malt beverage license, all such licensees agree to the conditions of this chapter and that all of their business records, including, but not limited to, till slips, purchase orders, receipts, deposit slips, checks, personal banking records, tax returns, tax records, and any and all other records relating in any way to the operation of liquor establishments and/or malt beverage establishments shall be open and made available for inspection by the City of Sisseton by and through its auditors, finance officer, attorney, police officers, mayor and council or other agents or representatives at any reasonable time by any law enforcement officer acting under color of his authority. 
    All water, sewer, garbage bills and other obligations to the City of Sisseton must be kept current. Being delinquent on any obligation to the City of Sisseton or being delinquent on real estate taxes at any time during the year shall constitute cause for non-renewal of a liquor license and/or malt beverage license or operating agreement. 
(Ord. No. 617, § II, 12-10-2012) 
5.08.030 - License to Sell Alcoholic Beverages and/or Malt Beverages. 
A.  The price of a license to sell alcoholic beverages within the City of Sisseton shall be set in the operating agreement between the liquor establishment and the City of Sisseton. 
B.  The price of on-sale and off-sale malt beverage licenses within the City of Sisseton shall be set from time to time by the State of South Dakota. 
C.  No license to sell alcoholic beverages or malt beverages within the City of Sisseton shall be issued until an application therefore has been filed with the City Finance Officer and the person, firm or corporation making said application has been duly approved by the city council. 
D.  Upon approval of the applicant by the city council, and payment by the applicant of the license fee in full to the City Finance Officer, the City Finance Officer shall issue a receipt for said payment, which receipt shall be treated as the applicant's license to operate. Said receipt shall at all times be posted in a conspicuous place in the licensee's place of business. 
(Ord. No. 617, § III, 12-10-2012) 
5.08.040 - Minors. 
A.  Sales or gifts of alcoholic beverages to minors are prohibited. No person shall within the city limits of the City of Sisseton give away, sell or in any manner provide intoxicating liquors or malt beverages to any person under the age of twenty-one (21) years or to any person intoxicated or who is in the habit of becoming intoxicated. 
B.  Minors are disallowed from the premises of liquor and malt beverage establishments. It shall be unlawful to allow any person under the age of twenty-one (21) years of age to enter, remain in or loiter in an on-sale liquor establishment or malt beverage establishment as well as to enter, remain in or loiter in the City Municipal Liquor Store. It shall be unlawful for any such under-aged person to attempt to gain entrance or enter said establishment or for any person to aid or abet any under-age person in an attempt to gain entrance to or enter into said establishment except as provided in the following instances: 
1.  This age restriction shall not apply to malt beverage licensees which obtain more than fifty (50) percent of their gross income from sources other than the sale of malt beverages. If said malt beverage establishment has a specific room exclusively for the sale of malt beverages, minors shall not be permitted to enter said room. 
2.  Minors shall be allowed to accompany their parent or parents or any adult so designated by their parent or parents into an on-sale liquor establishment or malt beverage establishment for the purpose of attending a wedding, anniversary or birthday dance or similar function. Minors shall be allowed to accompany their parent or designated person into a restaurant, supper club or other business that serves to the public, even though said business has an on-sale liquor license or malt beverage license. No minor shall be allowed to consume alcoholic beverages or malt beverages while attending any function or business described in this section, even in the presence of the parent or parents or the designated person. 
3.  Minors shall be allowed to enter a bowling alley even though said bowling alley shall have an on-sale liquor license or malt beverage license. If said bowling alley has a specific room exclusively for the sale of liquor or malt beverages, minors shall not be permitted to enter said room. No minor found to be in a bowling alley shall be allowed to consume alcoholic beverages or malt beverages even in the presence of the parent or parents. 
C.  The City Council may grant a variance from any portion of this section upon good cause being shown and not being in conflict with State Law. This variance shall be granted upon good cause being shown. The variance shall be granted for a period not to exceed one year. Any violation of the conditions under which said variance is granted shall be grounds for immediate cancellation of the variance and for any other action deemed necessary by the City. 
(Ord. No. 617, § IV, 12-10-2012) 
5.08.050 - Hours of business-Sales restricted to premises. 
A.  Malt Beverage License-Hours On-Sale. 
1.  It is unlawful for any on-sale light wine or malt beverage licensee or his or her agent(s) or employee(s) to sell, serve or allow to be consumed on the licensed premises within the city, any malt beverage, wine or other alcoholic beverages between the hours of 1:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. of the same day with the exception that the hours of on-sale business on Sundays shall be between the hours of 11:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. (midnight) on Sunday. No on-sale light wine or malt beverage licensee shall sell, serve or allow to be consumed on the licensed premises, any malt beverages, wine or other alcoholic beverage at any time on Christmas Day, or permit in the building where the business is carried on, any malt beverage, wine or other alcoholic beverage to be sold or consumed during the prohibited hours, except as hereinafter provided. 
2.  It is unlawful for any on-sale dealer of malt beverages, wine or other alcoholic beverages to allow such to be sold, mixed or consumed on the premises occupied by the dealer during any of the hours in which the sale of the malt beverage, wine or other alcoholic beverage is prohibited. 
B.  Liquor Licenses-Hours On-Sale. 
1.  It shall be unlawful for any on-sale liquor licensee, his agent(s) or employee(s) to sell, serve or allow to be consumed on the licensed premises, within the City of Sisseton, any alcoholic beverage between the hours of 1:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. of the same day with the exception that the hours of on-sale business on Sundays shall be between the hours of 11:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. (midnight) on Sunday. No on-sale liquor licensee shall sell, serve or allow to be consumed on the licensed premises, any malt beverages, wine or other alcoholic beverage at any time on Christmas Day. 
a.  Each licensee desiring a Sunday on-sale liquor license shall apply for such license with the City Finance Officer and pay a fee of $200.00 for such license which fee shall be submitted with said application. 
C.  Malt Beverage and Liquor Licenses-Off Sale. It shall be unlawful for any off-sale malt beverage or liquor licensee, their agent(s) or employee(s) to sell any alcoholic beverages between the hours of 1:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. of the same day with the exception that the hours of off-sale business on Sundays shall be between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. (midnight) on Sunday. All alcoholic beverage and/or malt beverage sold off-sale must be out of the licensed premises by 1:00 a.m. with the exception of Sunday sales which must be out of the licensed premises by 12:00 a.m. (midnight) on Sunday. No off-sale malt beverage or liquor licensee shall sell any malt beverages, wine or other alcoholic beverage at any time on Christmas Day. 
D.  Special Events Licenses. The City of Sisseton has authority to issue a special alcoholic beverage license in accordance with SDCL 35-4-124, as amended from time to time. The applicant must make their request for a special alcoholic beverage license in writing to the Finance Officer setting forth the special event for which said license is requested, which type of alcoholic beverage license is requested, and the date and times of operation. The Finance Officer shall present the written request for special alcoholic beverage license to the City Council. The City Council shall determine whether or not to grant the special alcoholic beverage license, and shall notify the applicant in writing as to the Council's decision. If the request for special event license is granted, the written permission shall designate which type of alcoholic beverage license(s) is/are granted, the date and specific hours within which the special alcoholic beverage license is granted, and the rules and/or restrictions related to the issuance of the special event license. A license fee in the amount of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for a malt beverage license, one hundred dollars ($100.00) for an on-sale wine license, and two hundred dollars ($200.00) for an on-sale liquor license shall be paid by the applicant upon approval of the special alcoholic beverage license. Each fee is individual to each license, and if more than one license is granted, the applicant must pay the total of the costs associated with licensing. A fee waiver will be considered by the City Council upon request by the applicant. The applicant must also present proof of insurance and hold the City harmless from any liability arising from the special event. 
E.  Unlawful to Remain on Premises After Closing. It shall be unlawful for any person, excluding employee(s), manager(s) and owner(s) to remain in an on- or off-sale malt beverage or liquor establishment after 1:30 a.m. It shall be unlawful for any employee(s), manager(s) and owner(s) to remain in an on- or off-sale malt beverage or liquor establishment after 2:10 a.m. without permission of a law enforcement officer. 
F.  Serving Alcoholic Beverages Outside of Building is Unlawful. It shall be unlawful for any on-sale dealer within the City of Sisseton to serve malt beverages, wine or other alcoholic beverages outside of the building or structure for which the license is issued. 
G.  Unlawful to Leave Establishment With Alcoholic Beverage in Possession-Exceptions. It shall be unlawful for an on-sale malt beverage establishment, a liquor establishment or any employee(s), manager(s) or owner(s) thereof to allow any person to leave the licensed premises within the City of Sisseton with any container of alcoholic beverage in their possession, except for the sale of unopened containers of malt beverage, where the licensee has sold the same under a malt beverage off-sale license. 
(Ord. No. 617, § V, 12-10-2012; Ord. No. 644, 6-12-2017) 
5.08.060 - Authority of Law Enforcement to Close Establishment. 
    If, in the opinion of a law enforcement officer, the conduct of individuals in an on-sale liquor establishment or malt beverage establishment constitutes a threat to the peace and safety of the citizens of the City of Sisseton, any such law enforcement officer may close said establishment for the remainder of the operating day. Such action and the reasons therefore must be promptly reported to the Mayor and the City Attorney. 
(Ord. No. 617, § VI, 12-10-2012) 
5.08.070 - Penalties. 
    Any person or on-sale liquor establishment or malt beverage establishment found to have violated this chapter shall be subject to: 
A.  A fine not to exceed two hundred dollars ($200.00) or a jail sentence not to exceed thirty (30) days or both. Each day of violation of this chapter shall constitute a separate violation. As to the sale of malt beverage not purchased through the municipal liquor store, each bottle or container sold shall constitute a separate offense. 
B.  The City Council, Chief of Police, City Attorney, Mayor, or Finance Officer may forward, without notice to the licensee, any alleged violation of this Ordinance directly to the South Dakota Secretary of Revenue for its review and potential implementation of additional penalties. 
(Ord. No. 617, § VII, 12-10-2012) 
Chapter 5.12 - DRUG PARAPHERNALIA 
Sections: 

5.12.010 - License required. 
    It is unlawful for any person or persons as principal, clerk, agent, or servant to sell any item, effect, paraphernalia, accessory, or thing which is designed or marketed for use with illegal cannabis or drugs, as defined by the South Dakota Codified Laws, without obtaining a license. Such licenses shall be in addition to any or all other licenses held by applicant. 
(Prior code § 7-3-1) 
5.12.020 - Application. 
    Application to sell any item, effect, paraphernalia, accessory, or thing which is designed or marketed for use with illegal cannabis or drugs shall, in addition to the other requirements of this chapter, be accompanied by affidavits by applicant and each and every employee authorized to sell such items that such person has never been convicted of a drug related offense. 
(Prior code § 7-3-2) 
5.12.030 - Fee. 
    The fee for such license shall be in an amount set by the city council and on file at the office of the finance officer. 
(Prior code § 7-3-3) 
5.12.040 - Minors. 
    It is unlawful to sell or give items as described in Section 5.12.060 in any form to any person under eighteen (18) years of age. 
(Prior code § 7-3-4) 
5.12.050 - Records. 
    Every licensee must keep a record of every item, effect, paraphernalia, accessory, or thing which is designed or marketed for use with illegal cannabis or drugs which is sold and this record shall be open to inspection of any police officer or Roberts County law enforcement officer at any time during the hours of business. Such record shall contain the name and address of the purchaser, the name and quantity of the product, the date and time of the sale, and the licensee or agent of the licensee's signature. Such records shall be retained for not less than two years. 
(Prior code § 7-3-5) 
5.12.060 - License guidelines. 
    Every license must adhere to these provisions regarding display of items. 
A.  Paper. White paper or tobacco oriented paper not necessarily designed for use with illegal cannabis or drugs may be displayed. Other paper of colorful design, or names oriented for use with illegal cannabis or drugs and displayed are covered. 
B.  Roach Clips. Roach clips are designed for use with illegal cannabis or drugs and therefore covered. 
C.  Pipes. Pipes if displayed away from the proximity of nonwhite paper or tobacco oriented paper, and not displayed within proximity of roach clips, or literature encouraging illegal use of cannabis or illegal drugs are not covered; otherwise, covered. 
D.  Paraphernalia. Other items and paraphernalia designed or marketed for use with illegal cannabis or drugs if displayed with roach clips or literature encouraging illegal use of cannabis or drugs are covered. 
(Prior code § 7-3-6) 
5.12.070 - Penalty. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount set forth in Chapter 1.16, and each day during which any person, firm, or corporation shall be engaged in business in violation of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed and constituted a separate and distinct offense. 
(Prior code § 7-3-7) 
Chapter 5.16 - JUNKYARDS AND JUNK DEALERS 
Sections: 

5.16.010 - Definitions. 
    The term "junkyard" means any area or lot where two or more unusable automobiles, old metal, rags, waste paper, green hides, or used electrical and/or gas appliances of all descriptions shall be loaded or stored. The term is also defined as any business for the sale or purchase of salvage material, goods, wares, or merchandise and secondhand goods, including motor vehicles and accessories for motor vehicles or a salvage or wrecking yard or store, also including used electrical and/or gas appliances of all descriptions. 
    The term "junk dealer" means any person or persons, firm, or corporation engaged in business as a dealer or trader of junk, rags, waste paper, old iron, brass, copper, tin, empty bottles, junked automobiles or parts thereof, used electrical appliances and/or gas appliances of all descriptions, or other articles which from worn condition are rendered useless for the purpose designed, or is engaged in whole or in part in the business of purchasing, processing, and selling used automobiles, motor vehicles, and other machinery which are brought to his or her place of business and cut and sorted in accordance with their metallic content and sold, or what is commonly known as salvage operations. 
(Prior code § 7-7-1) 
5.16.020 - Junkyard maintained within city limits. 
    No building, place, or lot where junk, junked automobiles, parts thereof, used electrical and/or gas appliances of all descriptions, or other worn-out machinery of any kind is bought, sold, or stored, shall be established or maintained within the city without special permission having been granted by the city council of the city. 
(Prior code § 7-7-2) 
5.16.030 - License required. 
    No person shall engage in business as a junk dealer or operate a junkyard within the city or within one mile thereof without first having secured a license. 
(Prior code § 7-7-3) 
5.16.040 - Application for license. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation desiring a license to operate as a junk dealer shall make application in writing to the city council and the application shall state: (a) name, post office address, and length of time applicant has resided in the city; (b) the premises where the business is or will be located or conducted, described by lot and block number or by legal description; (c) any other information the city council may require. 
(Prior code § 7-7-4) 
5.16.050 - Annual fee. 
    Every junk dealer or operator of a junkyard shall pay an annual fee as shall be set by resolution of the city council for each establishment or place of business which shall include one junkyard, and a further fee as shall be fixed by the city council for each additional junkyard, and the operator of the junkyard shall at all times keep the junkyard and his or her place of business in such condition so that the same will not become offensive or obnoxious, and the premises shall at all times be free of rodents. 
(Prior code § 7-7-5) 
5.16.060 - Municipal finance officer to issue license. 
    Upon filing of the application together with the necessary license fee, the council, if they deem such applicant a fit and proper person to engage in such business, may by majority vote grant such license and thereupon such license shall be issued by the finance officer in the manner provided for the issuance of licenses. 
(Prior code § 7-7-6) 
5.16.070 - Revocation of license. 
    The city council has the right to revoke any license granted under this chapter if it determines upon investigation and after hearing that the licensee has violated any of the provisions of this chapter, provided that notice of the hearing shall be served upon the licensee named in the license at least five days before the hearing, either by personal service of a copy of the notice or by mailing a copy of the same to the person at the address given in the application. Should any license granted under this chapter be revoked, no refund of the license fee shall be made. 
(Prior code § 7-7-7) 
5.16.080 - Daily record of purchases. 
    Every junk dealer shall keep a daily written record of all articles and quantities purchased by him or her setting forth the name, residence, age, and occupation of the person from whom each article or articles were purchased and the name of the employer of such person, the date and hour the purchase was made, the price paid, and such other information as the chief of police with the approval of the city council requires. Such record shall at all times be opened for the inspection of police officers or any officer of the law to make investigation and also for securing evidence in connection with any violation of law. 
(Prior code § 7-7-8) 
5.16.090 - Written report to chief of police upon request. 
    Every junk dealer upon being served with written notice to do so by a member of the police department, shall report to the chief of police, giving a written description of all goods, articles, and things purchased or received by him or her in the course of business as a junk dealer and covering such a period of time as may be specified in the notice. Such written report shall state the amount paid for each item and the name, residence, and general description of the person from whom the goods, articles, or things were received. 
(Prior code § 7-7-9) 
5.16.100 - Restrictions of operations. 
A.  No junk dealer shall carry on a business at or from any other place than the premises designated and described in the application and license, and all junk of any kind described shall be kept wholly within the boundaries of such premises. 
    It is unlawful for any junk dealer to burn junk or refuse on the premises covered by such license or any other place within the city. 
C.  The wrecking and dismantling of old cars for the purpose of securing parts shall be done wholly inside of the buildings occupied by the junk dealer or within an enclosure and shall not occur upon any highway or city street or alley or outside of the premises described in the application and license. 
D.  In all cases where the business of a junk dealer is to be conducted on a vacant lot or lots or in a partially enclosed structure, the council shall have the right to inspect and determine whether or not the appearance of the lot or lots distract from the sightliness of the area in which such premises may be located, and in the event the council finds that the appearance of the lot or lots does distract from the appearance of the area in which located, no license shall be granted until such lot or lots have an enclosure with a tight, well constructed and well painted fence of at least ten (10) feet in height or of a sufficient height to cut off the public view and must not be located nearer than one hundred fifty (150) feet from any state or federal highway. After the construction of such fence it shall at all times be suitably maintained and kept in good repair by the licensee. 
E.  In no event shall any licensee permit any advertising matter of any sort to be placed upon the fence, except that such licensee may use and not exceed fifty (50) square feet of the fence for the purpose of advertising his or her business. 
F.  No goods, material, wares, merchandise, motor vehicles, or accessories for motor vehicles or any salvage goods, wares, merchandise, or materials including used electrical and/or gas appliances of all descriptions shall be kept, stored, or placed for a longer period than one day outside of such building or fence. 
(Prior code § 7-7-10) 
5.16.110 - Penalty. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation violating this chapter shall be fined according to the penalties described in Chapter 1.16 
(Prior code § 7-7-11) 
5.16.120 - Purchasing junk from minors. 
    It is unlawful for any person or persons, firm, or corporation to purchase or receive from any person under the age of eighteen (18) years any article, goods, or things commonly known and classed as junk, any bottle, pipe or pipe fittings, lead, iron or brass, tools or implements, or any goods or wares of a secondhand character, or any rubber, overshoes, boots, or rubber goods of any nature, either secondhand or new without the written consent of such minor's parent or guardian, which writing shall be kept by such person or persons, firm, or corporation and be subject to the inspection of any police officer of the city. 
(Prior code § 7-7-12) 
5.16.130 - Junkyard in areas where children play. 
    It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to leave unattended or to abandon in any public place or in any location that is accessible to children within the city limits of the city, or any location which is in plain view from adjacent property and from the public streets and alleys within the city, any junked cars, car bodies, wrecked cars, abandoned and unusable cars or bodies therefrom, and any other unsightly trash or junk which would be dangerous for children to play in, around, or upon and which is or tends to be unsightly and which does lower or tends to lower the value of adjacent property because of its unsightliness, unless those responsible for parking, abandoning, or leaving the old car bodies, junked cars, wrecked cars, or other unsightly junk first build a solid fence at least ten (10) feet in height around the area in which the junked cars, old car bodies, and other junk is to be placed, the fence to have a gate thereon to be securely fastened so small children cannot get in or among the old cars, junked cars, car bodies, or other junk where they could or may be injured. 
(Prior code § 7-7-13) 
Chapter 5.20 - MOTOR CARRIERS OF PASSENGERS 
Sections: 

5.20.010 - License required. 
    No person or corporation shall engage in the transportation of passengers by motor carrier upon the public highways from place to place within the City, without procuring a license therefore from the City. The City Council shall have authority to deny or revoke said license based upon cause. 
(Ord. 433 § 1, 1987) 
(Ord. No. 645, 8-28-2017) 
5.20.020 - Application for license. 
    Application for license shall be accompanied by proof that the applicant has complied with the laws of the state of South Dakota in relation to such occupation and by an undertaking or indemnity insurance , to be approved by the City Council, obligating the applicant to pay and final judgment not exceeding the sum of two hundred and fifty thousand dollars ($250,000.00) for property damage; two hundred and fifty thousand dollars ($250,000.00) for accidental death or injury to a person and not exceeding five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00) for accidental death or injury in one accident to more than one person, which undertaking or insurance shall be in force for the license period and may only be cancelled on ten (10) days notice to the City Council and shall terminate on full termination of the applicants engagement as a public motor carrier unless new undertaking or indemnity insurance is furnished to take effect forthwith on termination of the former undertaking or indemnity insurance. 
(Ord. 433 § 2, 1987) 
5.20.030 - License fee. 
    The license fee for the period of one year, commencing and ending on July 1st of each year, for the first vehicle shall be twenty-five dollars ($25.00) and for each additional vehicle ten dollars ($10.00). The license for any part of a year shall be the same as for a year. 
(Ord. 433 § 3, 1987) 
5.20.040 - License transfers. 
    On written request of the licensee and proposed transferee and the approval of the City Council such license may be transferred to another person or corporation. 
(Ord. 433 § 4, 1987) 
5.20.050 - License number. 
    License number shall be affixed to the licensed vehicle in a conspicuous place and there maintained during the licensed period. 
(Ord. 433 § 5, 1987) 
5.20.060 - Prohibitions. 
    No alcoholic beverages or controlled substances shall be allowed to be transported in any vehicle licensed under this chapter except that paying passengers may transport unopened alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. 433 § 6, 1987) 
5.20.070 - Inspections. 
    All vehicles operated as motor carriers of passengers under this chapter shall be subject to inspection of mechanical and physical condition and subject to search at any time by any law enforcement officer having jurisdiction in Roberts County. Applicant agrees to these conditions as a condition of his or her license. Any license granted hereunder may be suspended for refusal to comply with this section. 
(Ord. 433 § 7, 1987) 
5.20.080 - Penalty. 
    Any violation of the terms and conditions of this chapter shall be punishable on conviction by a fine not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) or imprisonment not to exceed thirty (30) days or both such fine and imprisonment. Each day of operation in violation of this chapter shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. 433 § 8, 1987) 
Chapter 5.24 - PAWNBROKERS AND SECONDHAND DEALERS 
Sections: 

5.24.010 - License required. 
    No person, firm, or corporation shall engage in the business of pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer within the city, without first obtaining a license to do so from the city finance officer. The application for such a license shall contain all pertinent information required by the finance officer and shall be issued and governed in accordance with this chapter, except secondhand goods dealers exempted under Section 5.24.030. 
(Prior code § 7-2-1) 
5.24.020 - Definitions. 
    "Pawnbroker" means any person, firm, or corporation who engages in the business of lending money on the deposit or pledge of personal property, other than the basis of action, securities, or evidence of indebtedness; or purchases personal property with an expressed or implied agreement or understanding to sell it back at a stipulated price. 
    Any pawnbroker may effect the purchase of secondhand personal property for resale purposes under the terms of this chapter by acquiring any pawn ticket of his or her own issued by transfer. 
    "Secondhand goods dealer" means any person, firm, or corporation, other than a pawnbroker or dealer in precious metals and precious gems, who purchases, collects, trades, sells, or deals in the following secondhand goods: business machines, tape recorders and tapes, all radio transmitters and receivers, musical instruments, cameras and camera accessories, power tools, sporting goods, stereos, stereo equipment and records, tools and tool boxes, television sets, weapons, bicycles, radios, microwave ovens, and jewelry. 
(Prior code §§ 7-2-2, 7-2-3) 
5.24.030 - Exceptions.
