    The definition of "secondhand goods dealer" shall exempt the following transactions: 
A.  Any person, firm, or corporation selling new, unused articles, and any receiving or taking in used articles or trade from the purchasers of the new articles against the purchase price of the new articles which are sold for their market value. 
B.  Any person collecting antique items of personal use only. 
C.  Casual and occasional sales of used household goods by the owner thereof to the public, on a non-receiving basis, if the seller, at time of sale, is now engaged for profit in the business of selling goods of that or a similar nature; this category includes those sales commonly referred to as "garage sales." 
D.  Any person, firm, or corporation dealing exclusively in the resale of used automobiles. 
E.  Any person, firm, or corporation that operates a junk yard for wrecked automobiles. 
F.  Transactions involving goods sold on consignment. 
G.  Transactions in secondhand goods at stores or events sponsored by nonprofit corporations or associations or fraternal or religious organizations. 
(Prior code § 7-2-3) 
5.24.040 - Identification required. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation applying for a pawnbroker's license or a secondhand goods dealer's license, must, before their application will be considered, come to the Sisseton Police Department and furnish adequate identification. No license under this chapter shall be issued to any person who has been convicted of a felony; no license under this chapter shall be issued to any corporation, one or more officers, or directors of which have been convicted of a felony. 
(Prior code § 7-2-4) 
5.24.050 - Bond required. 
    Each pawnbroker doing business in the city shall furnish a good and sufficient bond, with a surety to be approved by the city council, in the sum of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), conditioned for faithful observance of this chapter and conditioned for the safekeeping or return of all articles held in pledge of such pawnbroker. 
(Prior code § 7-2-5) 
5.24.060 - Separate license and bond for each place of business. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation conducting several or separate places of business shall pay the appropriate license fees and procure the appropriate licenses and bond for each place of business. The above mentioned proprietor's license shall be sufficient for all clerks, agents, and employees engaged at the place named in the license. 
(Prior code § 7-2-6) 
5.24.070 - Suspension, revocation of license. 
    A license issued to a licensee under this chapter, who has violated the provisions of this chapter, may be suspended for a prescribed period, or revoked in the event of failure on the part of the licensee to comply with the provisions of this chapter after ten (10) days written notice and a public hearing. 
(Prior code § 7-2-7) 
5.24.080 - Fixed premises. 
A.  No person shall engage in business as a pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer unless the person has a fixed premises where the business is conducted, either on a continuing basis or from time to time, and unless the person has first obtained a license to engage in that business at that premises. 
B.  For the purpose of this section, "fixed premises" shall include any nonmobile premises where such business is conducted and the pawned or purchased secondhand articles are held, whether or not that premises remains in the same location during the period the license is in effect. 
(Prior code § 7-2-8) 
5.24.090 - Change in location of licensed premises. 
    If, during the effective period of a license issued under this chapter, a pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer changes the location of the licensed premises within the city, such dealer shall inform the city finance officer of such change of location and shall have the new premises to be licensed noted on the license. There shall be no additional fee charged for changing the location of the licensed premises. 
(Prior code § 7-2-9) 
5.24.100 - Records required of pawnbrokers. 
    Every pawnbroker shall keep books or records of pawn tickets in a manner satisfactory to the chief of police, where he or she shall accurately and intelligibly enter, in ink, in the English language, at the time of purchasing or receiving any personal property, and after requiring and observing identification from the person seeking to pawn the property, a record of the following information: 
A.  The name of the person from whom the property is purchased or received, his or her place of residence, and his or her date of birth; 
B.  A detailed and accurate description of each article, which shall include, if available, the manufacturer's name, style, model number, serial number, engraved initials, or other identifying marks; 
C.  The date and time of transaction; 
D.  The amount necessary for redemption; 
E.  The date when the article is to be redeemed; 
F.  Any mortgage or bill of sale taken, or receipt of pawn ticket given. 
    Every pawnbroker shall also record the date of disposition or redemption from pawn of the article or any part or portion thereof. The disposition report shall be located in the same book and at the same place where the receiving records of the article are located. 
(Prior code § 7-2-10) 
5.24.110 - Records required of secondhand goods dealer. 
    Every secondhand goods dealer shall keep books or records for those articles listed in Section 5.24.020 in a manner satisfactory to the chief of police or his or her designee, where he or she shall accurately and intelligently enter, in ink, in the English language, at the time of purchasing or receiving any article or item, the following information: 
A.  The name of the person from whom the property was purchased or received, his or her place of residence, and his or her date of birth; 
B.  Date and time of the transaction; 
C.  A detailed description of the item which shall include, if available, the manufacturer's name, style, model number, serial number, engraved initials, or other identifying marks; 
D.  If the seller is not known personally to the dealer or the dealer's agent, the dealer is required to obtain the person's drivers license number and the state of issuance or, if available, the identifying number from at least one form of government issued identification; 
E.  The amount paid for the article. 
(Prior code § 7-2-11) 
5.24.120 - Copy of records delivered to the chief of police. 
    It shall be the duty of every pawnbroker or dealer in secondhand goods to make out and deliver on the 1st and 15th of each month to the chief of police, a legible and correct copy of all records of personal property or other valuable things received, deposited, purchased, or placed on consignment during the preceding time period. The records provided to the chief of police shall include the following: 
a.  The time when the personal property or other valuable thing was received, deposited, purchased, or consigned; 
b.  A serial number or other identifying number for any item of personal property or other valuable thing received, deposited, purchased, or consigned with a serial number or other identifying number; 
c.  A description of the person or persons, and clear, color photograph of one legal form of picture identification of the person or persons by whom such article was left in pledge or from whom the same was purchased or taken on consignment. 
(Prior code § 7-2-12) 
(Ord. No. 615, 9-10-2012) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 615, adopted Sept. 10, 2012, amended § 5.24.120 title to read as herein set out. Former § 5.24.120 title pertained to copy of records delivered daily to chief of police. 
5.24.130 - Inspection of records or license and pledged property. 
    The books or records required to be kept by pawnbrokers or secondhand goods dealers shall be open to the inspection of city police officers during reasonable business hours. The pawnbroker shall produce and show any article pledged in connection with any loan. The licenses required for pawnbrokers or secondhand goods dealers shall at all times be on display in a conspicuous place and available for inspection by city police officers during reasonable business hours, unless the license is being taken to the city finance officer to have a change of location recorded. 
(Prior code § 7-2-13) 
5.24.140 - Penalty for misrepresenting transactions. 
    Any person who fails to keep such records or fails to make the required entries therein, or shall intentionally or knowingly make any false or unintelligible entry, or any entry which he or she has reason to believe is untrue, or who shall fail to make the inquiries necessary to enable him or her to make such entries, or who shall fail to produce his or her records when requested by a city police officer during reasonable business hours, or who shall destroy or willfully permit such records to be destroyed or lost, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and subject to the penalty provisions of Chapter 1.16. 
(Prior code § 7-2-14) 
5.24.150 - Length of records to be kept. 
    The records required by this chapter shall be maintained for one year after the date of purchase or receipt and shall be made available for inspection to city police officers during reasonable business hours. 
(Prior code § 7-2-15) 
5.24.160 - Pawn tickets. 
    At the time of receiving a pledge and upon the subsequent renewal of a loan, the pawnbroker shall deliver to the pledgor or his or her agent a pawn ticket, which pawn tickets shall be correspondingly serially numbered, and shall contain the following information: the name and address of the pawnbroker; a generic description of the pledge with such particular details of description noted whenever possible in order to distinguish the article or articles; the date and time of the transaction, and the amount, duration, and terms of the loan. The pawnbroker may insert on the pawn ticket any other terms, conditions, and information that are not inconsistent with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Prior code § 7-2-16) 
5.24.170 - Holding period for pawnbroker purchases. 
    Any licensed pawnbroker who shall purchase any new or secondhand goods of any individual not engaged in trade, shall keep the same for inspection for ten (10) days from the time of the transfer, except on written release from the chief of police or his or her designee. The above-mentioned property shall be held during this period on the licensed premises or some other secure location within the city and shall not be disposed of or altered from the form in which it was received during this period. 
(Prior code § 7-2-17) 
5.24.180 - Holding period of secondhand goods-Exceptions. 
A.  Any person licensed as a secondhand goods dealer who shall purchase any new or secondhand goods as stated in Section 5.24.020 of any individual not engaged in trade shall either keep the same for inspection for ten (10) days from the time of transfer, except on written release from the chief of police or his or her designee, or, keep the same for three working days, excluding Saturdays, Sundays, and calendar holidays, after delivering the required records to the Sisseton Police Department. The above mentioned property shall be held during this period in the licensed premises or some other secure location within the city and shall not be disposed of or altered from the form in which it was received, except on written release from the chief of police or his or her designee. 
B.  When articles are acquired by a pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer in a group, they shall be kept together for identification purposes and not separated until the ten (10) day period has elapsed, unless released prior on written authorization by the chief of police or his or her designee. 
(Prior code § 7-2-18) 
5.24.190 - Pawned articles to be held forty (40) days. 
    Every article of any kind or description which is taken in pawn by a pawnbroker shall be held by the pawnbroker for a period of forty (40) days, during which time the same shall not be shown either for sale or for inspection, to any person, other than a city police officer, during reasonable business hours. 
(Prior code § 7-2-19) 
5.24.200 - Effect of hold order. 
    The chief of police or any authorized police officer may, by written order, order a pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer to hold any specified article or articles, deposited with or in custody of such pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer, for purposes of further investigation by the police department, when the item or items are believed to be stolen. A hold order shall remain in effect for a period of thirty (30) days commencing the day on which the hold order was delivered to the pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer. A hold order shall supersede the provisions of Sections 5.24.170 and 5.24.180 of this chapter, and no sale or other disposition may be made of the article or articles while such hold order remains outstanding, unless released by officers issuing the hold order. 
(Prior code § 7-2-20) 
5.24.210 - Accepting articles from other than lawful owner. 
    A pawnbroker who accepts in pledge any article as security for a loan from a pledgor who is not the owner thereof, obtains no property in the article, either by reason of maturation of the loan or by transference of the pawn ticket to the pawnbroker by the pledgor or holder thereof. Ignorance of the fact that the pledged article was lost or stolen shall not be construed to affect the question of title, and if the pawnbroker shall sell such article to a third person, he or she shall remain liable to the original owner. 
(Prior code § 7-2-21) 
5.24.220 - Transactions with minors which are unlawful. 
    It is unlawful for any pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer to accept any articles in pawn or purchase any secondhand personal property by acquiring a pawn ticket by transference from any person under eighteen (18) years of age. 
(Prior code § 7-2-22) 
5.24.230 - Concealing articles to prevent identification. 
    No pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer shall conceal, secrete, or destroy, for the purpose of concealing, any article purchased or received by him or her, for the purpose of preventing identification thereof by city police officers. 
(Prior code § 7-2-23) 
5.24.240 - Firearms. 
    No pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer shall purchase, accept as security, or retain in his or her possession, a firearm unless he or she shall obtain the name, age, and address from the person or persons from whom it was received and be able to give a physical description of the person or persons. The name, age and address shall be verified by the presentation of identification to the pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer. 
(Prior code § 7-2-24) 
5.24.250 - Examination of premises by city police officers. 
    No pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer or any other personnel shall refuse, resist, or attempt to prevent any city police officer without a warrant from examining the licensed premises occupied by the pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer, or other secured premises within the city limits where property is stored, during reasonable business hours for the purpose of discovering stolen property. 
(Prior code § 7-2-25) 
5.24.260 - Hours of operation. 
    No pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer covered under this chapter shall operate his or her business before 9:00 a.m. and shall cease operation of his or her business at or before the hour of 10:00 p.m. The pawnbroker or secondhand goods dealer shall post a sign on his or her place of business which shall be of sufficient size to be readable from the street listing the hours of business. 
(Prior code § 7-2-26) 
5.24.270 - Exemption. 
    The chief of police is authorized to issue a certificate of exemption, exempting a secondhand goods dealer from the requirements of this chapter where it is determined that the dealer makes a majority of his or her purchases outside of the city and a majority of his or her sales outside the city. Such exemption shall state whether it is an exemption from all portions of this chapter or an exemption from certain sections of this chapter. If the exemption is partial, it shall specifically state which sections of the chapter are covered by the exemption. An exemption shall be valid for one year and requests for renewal shall be directed to the chief of police. 
(Prior code § 7-2-27) 
Chapter 5.28 - PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS 
Sections: 

5.28.010 - Public nuisance. 
    The practice of going in and upon private residences, and premises in the city by solicitors, peddlers, hawkers, itinerant merchants and transient vendors and purchasers of merchandise, not having been expressly requested or invited to do so by the owners, occupant or occupants, of the private residences or premises, for the purpose of the sale or purchase of goods, wares, or merchandise, and for the soliciting of orders for the sale or purchase of the same, and for the purpose of disposing of, peddling or hawking the same, is declared to be a public nuisance, and punishable as such nuisance as a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. 143 § 1, 1937) 
5.28.020 - Abatement. 
    The chief of police and police department of the city are required and directed to suppress the same, and to abate any such nuisance as is described in the Section 5.28.010. 
(Ord. 143 § 2, 1937) 
5.28.030 - Violation-Penalty. 
    Any person convicted of perpetrating a nuisance as described and prohibited in the Section 5.28.010, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined in a sum not less than twenty-five dollars ($25.00), nor more than one hundred dollars ($100.00), together with costs of proceedings, which the fine may be satisfied, if not paid in cash, by execution against the person of anyone convicted of committing the misdemeanor herein prohibited. 
(Ord. 143 § 3, 1937) 
Chapter 5.32 - TRANSIENT MERCHANTS 
Sections: 

5.32.010 - Locally-raised produce. 
    Persons selling farm produce raised locally shall be granted a license without any fee. 
(Ord. 438 § 1, 1988) 
5.32.020 - Other produce. 
    Other than as described in Section 5.32.010, persons selling farm produce shall pay a license fee of five dollars per year. 
(Ord. 438 § 2, 1988) 
5.32.030 - Home businesses. 
    Persons selling merchandise, insurance, investments, goods or wares from their homes as their principal places of business shall, if their homes are located within thirty (30) miles of the city limits, be granted licenses without fee. 
(Ord. 438 § 3, 1988) 
5.32.040 - Other businesses. 
    Persons selling any and all merchandise, insurance, investments, goods or wares not covered by Sections 5.32.010-5.32.030 shall be subject to a license fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) per year. 
(Ord. 438 § 4, 1988) 
5.32.050 - Duration of license. 
    Licenses shall run from January 1 to December 31 and the fee shall not be pro-rated for any part of a year, but shall be due and payable in full. 
(Ord. 438 § 5, 1988) 
5.32.060 - Violation-Penalty. 
A.  Operating without a license shall be a class 2 misdemeanor punishable by a maximum of a one hundred dollar ($100.00) fine. 
B.  Each day that a person operates without a license as hereinbefore set forth constitutes a separate violation. 
(Ord. 438 §§ 6, 7, 1988) 
Chapter 5.36 - MISCELLANEOUS BUSINESS REGULATIONS 
Sections: 

5.36.010 - Carnivals and circuses. 
    It is unlawful for any person or persons owning, managing, or operating any circus, menageries, wild west shows, carnival, or other exhibition to exhibit in the city without first registering with the city finance office the nature and purpose of the activity, the hours of operation, the length of time appearing, and the particular place to be used. Such shows or exhibits must be approved by the city council which may require that a bond be filed to cover the cost of cleanup or repair. 
(Prior code § 7-4-1) 
5.36.020 - Video lottery machines. 
    Each video lottery machine in use in the city shall be subject to an annual fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) per machine to the city. This fee shall be payable on or before January 15th of each year by the holder of the alcoholic beverage license having the machine or machines on the premises. Any new machines installed after the due date shall pay a pro-rata fee based on the day they are placed in service. All annual video lottery machine fees shall be payable to the city finance officer. 
(Ord. 475, 1992) 
Title 6 - ANIMALS 
Chapter 6.04 - ANIMALS GENERALLY 

6.04.010 - Cruelty to animals. 
    Any person who in the city cruelly or immoderately beats any horse, mule, cow, or other animal, or neglects to properly take care of or feed any such animals, or leaves standing in the streets any horse, mule, team, or other animals, unprotected an unreasonable time, or who overworks, overloads, or overdrives any horse or other working animal, shall upon conviction be fined in any sum not less than five dollars nor more than one hundred dollars ($100.00); and the chief of police or any police officer shall take such action as may be necessary for the immediate protection of the animal or animals. 
(Prior code § 8-4-1) 
6.04.020 - Inciting animals to fight. 
    Any person who in the city by words, signs, or otherwise, sets any animal or animals to fighting, or to attack any other animal or animals, or who aids and abets or encourages any animal fight, or any owner, keeper or harborer of any animal, who knowingly permits such animal to fight without endeavoring to prevent the same, or to any person who by signs, words, or otherwise sets on or encourages any animal to attack or chase any human being not engaged in any malicious act, shall, upon conviction be fined in any sum not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00). 
(Prior code § 8-4-2) 
6.04.030 - Animals running at large. 
    No hogs, cattle, horses, mules, sheep, geese, or poultry are permitted to run at large in the streets, alleys, or public places within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Prior code § 8-4-3) 
6.04.040 - Pound master-Created. 
    The office of pound master is created and established. 
(Prior code § 8-4-4) 
6.04.050 - Pound master-Duties. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police or the pound master, and they are hereby authorized and empowered to distrain all hogs, cattle, horses, mules, sheep, geese, or poultry running at large, or picketing or pasturing in the streets, alleys, or public places within the corporate limits of the city contrary to the provisions of this chapter, and to safely keep the same in the public pound until the same shall be claimed or disposed of as provided by this chapter. 
(Prior code § 8-4-5) 
6.04.060 - Public notices posted. 
A.  The chief of police or pound master shall within twenty-four (24) hours (Sunday excluded) after distraining any such animals or fowls, give public notice of such distraint and of the time and place of sale thereof, by posting with written or printed notices of such distraint and sale, in three public places within the corporate limits of the city. 
B.  These notices shall describe such animals or fowls distrained with reasonable certainty and shall state the time and place of sale, which sale shall not take place within less than three days, or more than six days from the time of posting the notices. 
C.  If the animals or fowls distrained shall in the opinion of the chief of police or pound master be of the value of twenty-five dollars ($25.00) or more, then notice of such distraint and sale shall be published in the official newspaper of the city, or posted in five public places within the corporate limits of the city for the period of two weeks successively. 
D.  Unless the owner shall sooner claim the the property distrained, and pay the expenses of distraining and keeping the animal to the pound master, together with the expenses of advertising, if there be any, and in case the property so distrained shall be, in the opinion of the pound master, of the value of more than twenty-five dollars ($25.00), and the owner thereof shall be known, then such pound master or chief of police shall give notice in writing personally to the owner thereof, of such distraint and sale, together with the time and place thereof, and any and all property distrained under and by virtue of this chapter. 
E.  Unless redeemed by payment as aforesaid prior to such sale the animal or fowl shall be sold by the pound master or chief of police at public auction, to the highest bidder for cash and shall pay over the surplus, if any there shall be to the municipal finance officer of the city, and, in case of a sale being made, he or she shall make a report in writing to the city council, which report shall describe the property sold, the time when sold, and place where distrained, the amount for which it was sold, together with the name of the owner, if known, the amount retained by him or her for fees, costs, and expenses, specifying each item separately, and the name of the purchases, at the first meeting of the city council occurring after such sale. 
(Prior code § 8-4-6) 
6.04.070 - Owner seeking proceeds after property is sold. 
    If any person or persons after the making of sale as aforesaid, shall satisfactorily prove to the city council that he or she or they were the owner of the property so sold, the city council may cause an order to be drawn on the municipal finance officer, signed by the mayor and countersigned by the finance officer, enabling the finance officer to pay such person or persons the net proceeds of the property sold, after deducting his or her fees for receiving and paying out the same, as provided by this chapter. 
(Prior code § 8-4-7) 
6.04.080 - Pound master penalized. 
    If the chief of police or pound master, shall willfully neglect or refuse to distrain and impound any of the animals or fowls described in this chapter running at large contrary to the provisions of this chapter, he or she shall for each offense, upon conviction thereof, be punished by a fine of five dollars, to be prosecuted for and enforced in the same manner that fines for the violation of the ordinances of the city are prosecuted for and enforced. 
(Prior code § 8-4-8) 
6.04.090 - Hindering or obstructing pound master. 
    The pound master or chief of police, in distraining the animals or fowl described in this ordinance, may when reasonably necessary, employ any assistance. Any person or persons who shall hinder or obstruct the pound master or anyone else so authorized from distraining any animal or fowl as provided in this chapter, shall for each such offense be punished by a fine of not more than ten dollars ($10.00) and costs of prosecution. 
(Prior code § 8-4-9) 
Chapter 6.08 - DOGS, CATS AND OTHER PET ANIMALS 

6.08.010 - License. 
    It is unlawful for any person or persons within the city to keep, maintain, or have in his or her custody or control, any dog or cat without first having obtained a license to do so from the city finance officer as hereinafter provided and without having paid the license fee therefor. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-1, 1999) 
6.08.020 - Application. 
    Any person or persons desiring to keep, maintain, or have in his or her custody or control by him or herself or agent, within the city, any dog or cat shall, on or before the first day of May of each year make application to the city finance officer for a license to keep such animal. Such application shall be in writing, stating the name, species, sex, color and other distinguishing characteristics of the animal and the name of the owner, and that the animal has no vicious propensities so far as known to the applicant, which application shall be made on a printed blank furnished by the city finance officer and shall be filed with the city finance officer. In addition, the applicant shall exhibit to the finance officer, a certificate by a registered veterinarian showing that such animal has been inoculated against rabies and that the inoculation will be effective during the period for which the animal is licensed. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-2, 1999) 
6.08.030 - Fee-Tag. 
A.  The applicants shall at the time of making such application, pay to the city finance officer a license fee for each male dog or cat, spayed female dog or cat and a license fee for each unspayed female dog or cat, and the license fees shall be set by the city council and on file at the office of the city finance officer. 
B.  The fee for the first two dogs and the first two cats registered by each owner shall be substantially lower than the fee charged if a party has over two dogs or two cats. 
C.  It shall be the duty of the city finance officer at the time of the issuance of the license herein provided for, to furnish and deliver to the applicant, a metallic tag for each animal for which such license is issued. This metallic tag shall be stamped or engraved the registered number of the animal and the year when registered, and it shall then be the duty of the owner of the animal to place a collar around the neck of the animal owned or kept by him or her, on which collar shall be securely fastened a metallic tag furnished by the city finance officer. In case of the loss of any tag issued, the city finance officer is authorized to issue a duplicate upon proof that the tag has been lost. 
D.  Any owner who fails to purchase a license for the animal shall be subject to a fine as set in Chapter 1.16. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-3, 1999) 
6.08.040 - Restrictions on the keeping of dogs and cats. 
A.  No person shall keep or allow to be kept more than three adult dogs or cats per household in a house or yard of a house which the person owns or controls or occupies within the city. 
B.  The keeping or operation of a kennel or other structure or device for the commercial breeding of dogs, cats or other animal pets within the city is forbidden. 
C.  All female dogs, cats or other animal pets physically capable of producing litters shall be kept in a building or enclosure so as to deny access to the female animal by males. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-4) 
6.08.050 - Vicious animals. 
A.  A vicious animal is: 
1.  Any animal which, when unprovoked, in a vicious or terrorizing manner approaches in apparent attitude of attack, or bites, inflicts injury, assaults, or otherwise attacks a human on the streets, sidewalks, or any public grounds or places; or 
2.  Any animal which, when unprovoked, in a vicious or terrorizing manner approaches in apparent attitude of attack, or bites, inflicts injury, assaults, or otherwise attacks a domestic animal while running at large, or while on the streets, sidewalks, or any public grounds or places; or 
3.  Any animal which, on private property, when unprovoked, in a vicious or terrifying manner approaches in apparent attitude of attack, or bites, or inflicts injury, or otherwise attacks a child under the age of majority, mailman, meter reader, serviceman, journeyman, delivery man, any other employed person, or human who is on the property by reason of permission of the owner or occupant of such property or who is on private property by reason of a course of dealing with the owner of such private property. 
B.  In the event animal bites, or breaks skin of a human or a domestic animal, the owner must provide proof of up-to-date rabies vaccinations, or the animal must be quarantined in the city pound for a period of ten (10) days at the owner's expense. Despite those requirements, if a medical professional determines the animal must be euthanized and tested for rabies, the medical professional's determination shall prevail over the prior options and the animal must be euthanized at the owner's or keeper's expense and tested for rabies at the owner's or keeper's expense. All animals under this paragraph must be removed from the city limits upon leaving quarantine, or immediately upon proof of up-to-date rabies vaccination. 
C.  No person or persons shall permit any animal, which he or she may be the owner or keeper of to be kept in the city after the owner or keeper has been informed that the animal is vicious, as defined above. The police department shall provide the owners or keepers of the vicious animals notice of removal upon determining that said animal is vicious. Said notice may be verbal or in writing. 
D.  If the owner or keeper fails to comply with the notice of removal by removing of the animal from the city limits of the city, within twenty-four (24) hours of receipt of such notice, the police are empowered and directed to take such animal into custody, whether found running at large or upon the premises of the owner or keeper, forthwith, without notice to the owner or keeper of the animal. The police shall have the full right to enter upon the premises of the owner or keeper, including all outbuildings, but not the owner's or keeper's home without consent or a search warrant, to make sure that any animal has been removed and by keeping any animal pet within the city limits of the city, the owner or person keeping or harboring the pet has agreed to this authority of the police department. Any animal taken into custody after the owner's failure or refusal to remove such animal shall first be attempted to rehome with the nearest animal shelter or the humane society. If the nearest animal shelter or the humane society refuses to accept the animal, the city shall have authority to have a licensed veterinary doctor euthanize the animal. The expense of the euthanization shall be borne by the owner of the animal. 
E.  Notwithstanding the above, no animal may be declared vicious if an injury or damage is sustained to any person who was committing a willful trespass or other tort upon premises occupied by the owner or keeper of the animal, or who was teasing, tormenting, abusing, or assaulting the dog or was committing or attempting to commit a crime unless the animal is rabid. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-5; Ord. No. 628, 8-11-2014) 
6.08.060 - Nuisance animals. 
A.  It is unlawful for any person or persons to permit or suffer to run at large within the city limits of the city, any dog, cat, or other animal pet, whether licensed or unlicensed. The owner or keeper shall have the dog, cat, or other animal pet contained on its property on a leash, or enclosed by a fence at all times. Any animal control officer, police officer or person of proper authority is hereby authorized and empowered to impound any such animal found running at large. Any dog, cat, or other pet animal violating this provision shall be defined as a nuisance animal. 
B.  Any licensed animal found running loose shall be held at the city pound or some other proper and suitable place for a period of three days. If the owner or keeper does not call for the animal within the three-day period, the animal shall be rehomed with the nearest animal shelter or the humane society. If the nearest animal shelter or the humane society refuses to accept the animal, the city shall have authority to have a licensed veterinary doctor euthanize the animal. The expense of the euthanization shall be borne by the owner or keeper of the animal. Any dog, cat, or other pet animal violating this provision shall be defined as a nuisance animal. 
C.  Any unlicensed animal found running loose shall be held at the city pound for a period of twenty-four (24) hours. If unclaimed within the twenty-four-hour period, the animal shall be rehomed with the nearest animal shelter or the humane society. If the nearest animal shelter or the humane society refuses to accept the animal, the city shall have authority to have a licensed veterinary doctor euthanize the animal. The expense of the euthanization shall be borne by the owner or keeper of the animal, if said persons can be ascertained. Any dog, cat, or other pet animal violating this provision shall be defined as a nuisance animal. 
D.  If an animal is found running at large and in the opinion of the animal control officer or police officer involved the animal cannot be captured, the animal is hereby declared to be a public nuisance. If, in the opinion of the animal control officer or police officer involved, the animal constitutes a threat to the health, safety or welfare of the citizens of the city, or their property or animals, the animal control officer or police officer may destroy the animal immediately if such action can be safely done. Any dog, cat or other pet animal violating this provision shall be defined as a nuisance and/or vicious animal. 
E.  Any animal suspected of having rabies, which has bitten, or in any way injured a person, shall be addressed as set forth in Section 6.08.050. 
F.  No person owning, keeping harboring, or having on property occupied by him or her, any dog, cat, or other animal licensed or unlicensed, confined on the premises or otherwise, shall suffer or permit the animal to disturb the peace and quiet of the neighborhood by making loud and/or unusual noises, or shall suffer or permit the animal to disturb the peace and quiet of the neighborhood by persistent or constant barking, howling, whining, snarling, growling, or any other offensive noise. 
G.  Upon complaint being made to the police department that any person owns or is keeping or harboring any animals which disturbs the peace as herein set forth, or is keeping or harboring any animals that are a nuisance as defined herein, the police department shall be empowered to take immediate possession of the animal and to impound the animal. The police department shall have the full right and authority to go on the premises where the animal is located, including outbuildings, but not homes without consent or a search warrant, to take possession of the animal and to impound it for a period of three days. Any animal taken into custody which the owner's or keeper's fail to pick up after the third day of confinement shall be rehomed with the nearest animal shelter or the humane society. If the nearest animal shelter or the humane society refuses to accept the animal, the city shall have authority to have a licensed veterinary doctor euthanize the animal. The expense of the euthanization shall be borne by the owner of the animal. 
H.  By keeping any animal pet within the city limits of the city, the owner or person keeping or harboring the pet has agreed to the authority of the police department as set forth in this chapter. The police department shall contact the owner or person keeping or harboring the animal and advise them of the complaint and location where the animal is being held. In addition to the impounding of the animal or other penalties prescribed, the owner of the animal and the occupant of the property on which the animal is being kept or harbored during the times that the animal is disturbing the peace, or a nuisance, shall be subject to a penalty as prescribed in Chapter 1.16 for disturbing the peace, or keeping a nuisance animal. 
I.  No person or persons shall permit any animal, which he or she may be the owner or keeper of to be kept in the city after five violations of this ordinance. The police department shall inform the owners or keepers that the animal has violated this ordinance five times and provide notice of removal from the city. Said notice may be verbal or in writing. 
J.  If the owner or keeper fails to comply with the notice of removal by removing the animal from the city limits of the city, within twenty-four (24) hours of receipt of such notice, the police are empowered and directed to take such animal into custody, whether found running at large or upon the premises of the owner or keeper, forthwith without notice to the owner or keeper of the animal. The police shall have the full right to enter upon the premises of the owner or keeper, including all outbuildings, but not the owner's or keeper's home without consent or a search warrant, to make sure that the subject animal has been removed. Any animal taken into custody after the owner's or keeper's failure or refusal to remove such animal shall first be attempted to rehome with the nearest animal shelter or the humane society. If the nearest animal shelter or humane society refuses to accept the animal, the city shall have authority to have a licensed veterinary doctor euthanize the animal. The expense of the euthanization shall be borne by the owner of the animal. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-6; Ord. No. 628, 8-11-2014) 
6.08.070 - Unlicensed dog or cat. 
    An animal control officer may enter upon the premises of the owner or person keeping or harboring any unlicensed dog or cat for the purpose of seizing the animal. In addition to the impounding of the unlicensed dog, or cat or other penalties prescribed, the owner and the occupant of the property on which the dog or cat is being kept or harbored during the time the animal is not licensed shall be subject to a penalty as prescribed in Chapter 1.16. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-7) 
6.08.080 - Treatment of impounded animal. 
    All animals captured and conveyed to the pound, as established by the city, shall be kept with humane treatment and supplied with sufficient food and water for a period of at least twenty-four (24) hours unless sooner reclaimed by the owner or keeper thereof as herein provided. When the owner or claimant of any animal so impounded shall desire to redeem the animal from the pound, the animal may be released upon payment to the person in charge of the pound of an amount set by the city council and on file at the office of the city finance officer and costs of keeping, and shall exhibit a license for such animal, issued in the manner herein provided, and the person in charge of the pound shall thereupon release the animal to the owner or claimant. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-8) 
6.08.090 - Penalty. 
    A court of competent jurisdiction shall have the authority to order the destruction or removal of an animal from the city limits of the city, where the animal has violated the terms of this chapter. In addition, the owner thereof shall be subject to the penalties in Chapter 1.16. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-9) 
6.08.100 - Ignorance does not excuse the offense. 
    Ignorance of the law is not a defense in any proceeding for violation of the provisions of this chapter, and the knowledge or lack of knowledge of this chapter shall be considered immaterial. 
(Ord. 511 § 7-6-11; Ord. No. 628, 8-11-2014) 
Chapter 6.12 - DOMESTIC PETS 

6.12.010 - Domestic pets-Restrictions. 
    It is unlawful for a person to: 
A.  Allow the accumulation of animal feces in any open area, run, cage, structure or yard wherein animals are kept or allowed, and to fail to remove or dispose of the feces at least once every seven-day period. 
B.  Fail to clean up and remove fecal matter deposited by his or her animal on public property of another before the owner leaves the immediate area where the fecal matter was deposited. 
C.  Fail to have in his or her possession the equipment necessary to remove his or her animal's fecal matter when accompanied by said animal on public streets, public property, or private property of others. 
D.  Have possession or control of any animal sick or afflicted with any infectious or contagious disease and fail to provide treatment for such infection or disease, or to permit such diseased or infected animal to run at large or to come in contact with persons or other animals, or to drink at any public watering trough or stream accessible to other animals. 
E.  An owner or keeper shall provide their animal with sufficient food and water, proper shelter, humane care and treatment, and veterinary care when needed. No person shall mistreat any animal or shall abandon any animal. 
F.  An owner or keeper shall keep their animal on a leash while on public streets, public property or private property of others. 
G.  An owner or keeper shall keep their animal confined on their property with either a fenced in yard, a run, cage, or on a leash at all times. 
H.  This chapter shall apply to any owner or keeper of an animal in the city limits. 
I.  The penalty for a violation of this ordinance shall be the general penalty set forth in Chapter 1.16. 
(Ord. 582, 2006; Ord. No. 628, 8-11-2014) 
Title 8 - HEALTH AND SAFETY 
Chapter 8.04 - BOARD OF HEALTH AND SAFETY 
Sections: 

8.04.010 - Establishment and appointment. 
    A board of health and safety is hereby established in and for the city. The board shall consist of five persons: the health and safety officer, who shall be appointed for three years, two members to be appointed for two year terms, and two members to be appointed for a one year term. Thereafter, all appointments shall be made at the first city council meeting in May of each year. Board members shall receive no compensation for their services, except as any actual and necessary expenses incurred by them in the fulfillment of their duties. 
(Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-1) 
8.04.020 - Duties of the board. 
    The board of health and safety shall make such recommendations, investigations and reports and shall carry out such directions concerning public health and safety matters as the state department of health or the city council may require or give, and shall enforce all statutes, ordinances and all lawful rules and regulations concerning public health and safety. All matters of public health and safety and sanitation, disease prevention, abatement or control shall be under the management, direction and control of the board. The board shall meet during January and July of each year and shall thereupon furnish the city council with a written report of its activities during the preceding six months. 
(Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-2) 
8.04.030 - Removal of offensive matter. 
    The board of health shall have power and authority to require any person or persons owning property within the city to remove all offensive, dangerous, or deleterious matter from the premises, and to that end shall have power and authority to enter upon any premises or into any building in the city to examine the same and in case there is found to be any offensive, dangerous, or deleterious matter or conditions in or on the premises, or in any building, may direct in writing the removal or correction thereof. If the owner shall neglect or refuse to abate the problem, and shall fail to do so for a period of twenty-four (24) hours after such notice, he or she, upon conviction thereof shall be subject to a fine of up to two hundred dollars ($200.00) and costs and up to thirty (30) days in jail and the cost to the city of removing, correcting, or having the condition removed or corrected. It shall be the duty of the chief of police, under the direction of the board of health, to remove, correct or otherwise abate such nuisance as soon as possible after the appeal period hereunder has elapsed or as soon as the order to abate has been upheld on appeal by the city council. 
(Ord. 533, 2002: Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-3) 
8.04.040 - Notices, citations and orders. 
    In order to carry out the intent of this chapter whenever a section provides that notices, citations and orders are to be made or served by the board of health and safety, such notices, citations and orders may be made and served in a like manner and with a like effect by the city council. 
(Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-4) 
8.04.050 - Right of noninterference. 
    It is unlawful to obstruct, interfere with or impede the health and safety officer or any member of the board of health and safety in the performance of their respective duties or to remove, mutilate or destroy any sign posted by order of the health and safety office of the board of health and safety relating to any area or building within the city without prior approval of the health officer or the city council. 
(Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-5) 
8.04.060 - Interpretation. 
    It is the intent of the city, by its city council, to delegate to the health and safety officer, and the board of health and safety, full and complete authority commensurate with their responsibilities under this chapter, the laws, charters and regulations of the city, and the state of South Dakota relating to the corporate limits of the city of Sisseton, South Dakota. 
(Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-6) 
8.04.070 - Right to appeal to the council. 
    In the event the owner, proprietor, occupant or agent of any premise feels that the order to abate issued by the health and safety officer or board of health and safety is unjust, untrue or unwarranted, he or she shall have ten (10) days from the order to request a hearing before the city council to determine the necessity for the order. If requested, the city council shall hold such hearing to determine the validity of the order to abate. 
(Ord. 456 (part), 1990: prior code § 6-1-7) 
Chapter 8.08 - CONTAGIOUS DISEASES 
Sections: 

8.08.010 - Isolations of persons. 
    The board of health shall have power within the limits of the city to isolate all persons suffering with contagious diseases, and to make, demand, and require of the county board of health to immediately remove and care for all the cases as are not proper charges on the city; and the board of health shall have power to make rules and regulations covering the subject of all contagious diseases and other matters concerning the public health. 
(Prior code § 6-2-1) 
8.08.020 - Powers of board and health officer. 
    The board of health shall have power and authority to enter any premises in the city in search of contagious diseases or of nuisances, and shall have power and authority to quarantine any premises within the city, wherein is located any person suffering with an infectious or contagious disease, and may remove any person therefrom who is found to be suffering from, suspected to be suffering from, or has been exposed to any infectious or contagious disease, and the board may placard the premises, as aforesaid with the placard of such design and color as shall be determined by the board of health and which shall warn all persons within the premises not to leave the same, and all other persons whomever not to enter the premises without the written consent of a member of the board of health; and every physician practicing in the corporate limits of the city shall immediately report by telephone, or otherwise, to the health officer every case of contagious or infectious disease arising in his or her practice, and shall also report every case he or she suspects to be contagious, and the physician shall within twenty-four (24) hours thereafter make a written report of the case, and the name of the disease, and source of contagion, if known, and the physician shall also make a written report to the board of health upon the termination of the disease, and any person violating this chapter, or violating the order of the board of health, shall upon conviction thereof be subject to the penalties in Chapter 1.16. 
(Prior code § 6-2-2) 
Chapter 8.12 - DUTCH ELM DISEASE 
Sections: 

8.12.010 - Possession of dead elm trees. 
    It is unlawful to keep or have in possession any dead elm trees or dead elm wood of any species. Bark shall be removed from any elm wood to be used as fireplace wood so as to prevent the European bark beetle from mating and using it as a place of habitation. 
(Prior code § 6-5-1) 
8.12.020 - Removal of dead elm trees. 
    It is unlawful to permit any diseased elm tree to be left on property. Any person having a diseased elm of any species shall cause the same to be removed through the procedures outlined herein. 
(Prior code § 6-5-2) 
8.12.030 - City forester. 
    There is hereby created the position of city forester whose duty is to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(Prior code § 6-5-3) 
8.12.040 - Abatement of nuisances created by dead trees. 
    The following procedures shall be followed in abating the nuisances created by dead elm wood or diseased elm trees: 
A.  Once a year in June, the city forester shall take a physical survey of all trees within the city limits of the city and report his or her findings to the city council. If a tree appears to be diseased, the forester shall take a sample of the tree and have the sample analyzed by the state for dutch elm disease. Should the sample be positive, the forester will notify the property owner of the tree's disease by certified letter and inform the owner that if the tree is not removed within ten (10) days after receipt of the letter, that the city will have the tree removed and bill the property owner. If the bill is not paid within six months, the unpaid balance will be assessed against the property owner's taxes. 
B.  Any person allowing dead elm wood to be on their property shall be warned by the forester and thereafter be held in violation of this chapter and subject to the penalties thereof. 
C.  No person shall interfere nor attempt to interfere with the city forester in the conduct of his or her duty. 
D.  No person shall be permitted to plant, transplant, or otherwise cause to be planted any type of elm tree within the city. 
(Prior code § 6-5-4) 
8.12.050 - Penalty. 
    Any person who violates any provision established herein for the abatement of dutch elm disease shall be subject to the penalties established in Chapter 1.16. 
(Prior code § 6-5-5) 
Chapter 8.16 - GARBAGE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL 
Sections: 

8.16.010 - Definitions. 
    "Garbage" means kitchen and table refuse and every accumulation of waste, animal, and vegetable matter that attends the preparation, cooking, and eating of food or the storage, handling, sale, or decay of food, or any other substance that is in the process of decay, which gives off an odor offensive to the senses. 
    "Garbage container" means a water tight metallic or plastic can, of not less than ten (10) or more than thirty (30) gallon capacity, having a handle on each side, covered with a tight fitting metal or plastic lid, which must be kept in a sanitary condition at all times, with the outside thereof free and clean of grease or decomposed matter, secured in such manner that it cannot be tipped over or spilled by dogs or marauders. 
    "Rubbish" means broken crockery, destroyed bottles, tin cans, pasteboard boxes, wooden boxes, paper, straw, leaves, and ashes. 
    "Rubbish container" means a box, crate, or can of such character that it can be readily handled and emptied by the city rubbish collectors and sufficiently tight so as to prevent the rubbish therein contained from being blown or strewn about, not to exceed thirty (30) gallon capacity. 
(Prior code §§ 6-3-1-6-3-4) 
8.16.020 - Garbage and rubbish must be deposited in containers. 
    The occupant of every private home or dwelling place, and the operator of every place of business in the city, is required to deposit and keep the garbage that accumulates each day upon his or her premises in a garbage container above defined, and to each day deposit and keep the rubbish that accumulates upon his or her premises in a rubbish container herein defined, provided that grass, leaves, or other material to be used as compost for fertilizer may be kept in a pit or closed container, until such time as it may be used, and barnyard manure must be kept in a tightly closed box or container not exceeding a period of one week. 
(Prior code § 6-3-5) 
18.16.025 - Littering or dumping garbage within city-Illegal use of garbage facilities-Penalty. 
    It shall be illegal for any person to throw or dump garbage, litter or refuse of any sort on any street, boulevard, sidewalk, alley, or any private or public land within the city. 
    It shall be illegal for any person to place garbage or refuse of any kind in any dumpster within the city if that person does not subscribe to garbage service from the city, unless that person is acting as the agent or employee of a person who does subscribe to city garbage service. 
    It shall be illegal for any person subscribing to garbage service from the city to haul garbage or refuse produced outside the city into the city to dispose of it in the city or to have an agent or employee do so. 
    It shall be illegal for anyone to place items other than garbage in any dumpster in the city. Tires, auto parts, machinery parts, dead animals or dead animal parts, trees, branches, waste oil, grass, leaves, furniture, appliances, lumber, shingles and concrete shall not be placed in any dumpster belonging to the city within the city. Business waste shall be disposed of only in the dumpster assigned to that business. 
    The penalty for violation of this section shall be a fine not to exceed two hundred dollars ($200.00) and a jail sentence not to exceed thirty (30) days or both. 
(Ord. 558, 2003) 
8.16.030 - Garbage must be wrapped. 
    All garbage shall be wrapped in paper, plastic, or other material so as to prevent as nearly as possible moisture from the garbage from coming in contact with the sides and bottom of the garbage container. 
(Prior code § 6-3-6) 
8.16.040 - Garbage and rubbish containers for multiple-family dwellings. 
    The proprietor or operator of each duplex, apartment house, or similar multiple-family dwelling shall furnish and maintain for the use of the tenants therein a sufficient number of garbage containers and rubbish containers to hold all garbage and rubbish that accumulates upon such premises in the course of a week, or he or she shall require the tenants upon the premises to furnish such containers. The place where the garbage and rubbish containers are located shall be kept in a clean and sanitary condition at all times. 
(Prior code § 6-3-7) 
8.16.050 - Collection. 
    The city council of the city shall cause to be collected and dispose of all garbage within the city, where found. Rules and regulations for the collection and disposal of the garbage from the lots, premises, and private or public places within the city are as provided by this chapter. The city council shall make suitable arrangements for the collection of garbage with city equipment operated by city employees. Each residence and business within the city shall be required to subscribe to and pay for city garbage service. If for any reason the owner of any such residence or business is dissatisfied with the municipal garbage service, or has needs in excess of the services, the city is able to provide, he or she is free to hire and pay for additional service from any authorized garbage hauler. Subscribing to such additional service shall not relieve any patron from responsibility to pay the city for garbage service. 
(Ord. 579, 2005: prior code § 6-3-8) 
8.16.060 - Duty of garbage collector. 
    It shall be the duty of the garbage collector to collect and dispose of all garbage within the city at such times and places as the city council shall direct. He or she shall thoroughly clean up all garbage in the immediate vicinity of the place from which the garbage is removed, and see that none of the garbage is dropped or liquid matter permitted to escape from the receptacles in which it is being hauled on the streets or alleys of the city, and shall keep all garbage receptacles emptied at whatever regular intervals may be deemed necessary. 
(Prior code § 6-3-9) 
8.16.070 - City customers. 
    Responsibilities of the city and the customer with regard to application and billings for garbage collection services are fully set forth in Chapter 13.04, Utility Services Generally. 
(Prior code § 6-3-10) 
8.16.080 - Hauling through streets. 
    No garbage shall be hauled through the streets or alleys of the city unless contained in a water-tight steel tank or other water-tight tank or receptacle. 
(Prior code § 6-3-11) 
8.16.090 - Unlawful to haul garbage without permit-Penalty. 
    It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to engage in the business of collecting or hauling garbage from any place in the city without first having been authorized to do so by the city council of the city. Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor; and upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to the penalties described in Chapter 1.16. 
(Prior code § 6-3-12) 
8.16.100 - Burning garbage and rubbish. 
    No person shall burn any garbage outside of a residence building or business building at any place in the city. 
(Prior code § 6-3-13) 
8.16.110 - Nuisance-Penalty. 
    Every accumulation of garbage or rubbish which is deposited, kept, burned, or transported any place in the city in violation of the provisions of this chapter is declared to be a public nuisance, and any person who maintains or permits the maintenance of the nuisance shall upon conviction be subject to the penalties established in Chapter 1.16. 
(Prior code § 6-3-14) 
Chapter 8.20 - NUISANCES GENERALLY 
Sections: 

8.20.010 - Public nuisance defined-Remedy. 
    A public nuisance consists in unlawfully doing an act, or omitting to perform a duty within the corporate limits of the city or in any public grounds or parks belonging to the city or within one mile of the corporate limits of the city, which act or omission either: 
A.  Annoys, injures, or endangers the comfort, repose, or safety of others; 
B.  Offends decency; 
C.  In any way renders other persons insecure in life, or in the use of private property. 
    A public nuisance is defined as a nuisance which affects at the same time an entire community or neighborhood, or any considerable number of persons, although the extent of the annoyance or damage inflicted upon the individuals may be unequal. 
    The remedies against a public nuisance shall be those prescribed by Section 21-10-5 of the South Dakota Codified Laws, this title, or by other statute. 
(Prior code § 8-7-1) 
8.20.020 - Nuisances-Defined and prohibited. 
    No person shall create, commit, maintain, or permit to be created, committed, or maintained any nuisance as defined herein. 
    Whatever is dangerous to human health, whatever renders the ground, the water, the air, or food a hazard or an injury to human health, and the following specific acts, conditions, and things are, each and all of them, hereby declared to constitute nuisances. 
A.  Imperfect Plumbing. Any imperfect, leaking, unclean, or filthy sink, water closet, urinal, or other plumbing fixture in any building, used or occupied by human beings. 
B.  Garbage and Refuse. Depositing, maintaining, or permitting to be maintained or to accumulate upon any public or private property, any household wastewater, sewage, garbage, tin cans, offal, or excrement, any decaying fruit, vegetables, fish, meat, or bones or any foul, putrid, or obnoxious liquid substance. 
C.  Impure Water. Any well or other supply of water used for drinking or household purposes which is polluted or which is so constructed or situated that it may become polluted. 
D.  Undressed Hides. Undressed hides kept longer than twenty-four (24) hours, except at the place where they are to be manufactured, or in a storeroom, or basement whose construction is approved by the health department. 
E.  Manure. The accumulation of manure. 
F.  Breeding Place for Flies. The accumulation of manure, garbage, or anything whatever in which flies breed. 
G.  Stagnant Water. Any excavation in which stagnant water is permitted to collect. 
H.  Poison Ivy. Permitting poison ivy to be or to grow upon any private property nearer than fifteen (15) feet from the sidewalk or any public street. 
I.  Dead Animals. For the owner of a dead animal or fowl to permit it to remain undisposed of longer than twenty-four (24) hours after its death. 
J.  Farm and Other Live Animals. The keeping of live farm animals which are deemed to include horses, cattle, swine, sheep, fowl, and other animals that are normally raised or kept on farms, the keeping of live wild animals, and the keeping of any live animal in a manner so as to cause a public nuisance within the city limits. This shall not apply to "rural property" as defined in SDCL 9-2lA which is within the municipal boundaries of the city unless such keeping of animals within rural property is deemed to constitute a public nuisance. 
K.  Polluting Bodies of Water. Throwing or leaving any dead animal or decayed animal or vegetable matter or any slops or filth whatever, either solid, or fluid into any pool of water. 
L.  Privies and Cesspools. Erecting or maintaining any privy or cesspool except such sanitary privies and cesspools, the plans of which are approved by the state health department. 
M.  Garbage Handling Improperly. Throwing or letting fall or permitting to remain on any street, alley, public ground, or highway, any manure, garbage, rubbish, filth, fuel, or wood while engaged in handling or removing any such substances. 
N.  Rodents. Accumulation of junk, old iron, automobiles, cement slabs, or parts thereof, or anything whatever in which rodents may live or breed or accumulate. 
O.  Bonfires in Public Places. Burning, causing, or permitting to be burned in any street, alley, or public ground any dirt, filth, manure, garbage, swept leaves, ashes, paper, rubbish, or material of any kind. 
P.  Rubbish on Street. The piling or depositing of any dirt, shavings, sawdust, leaves, ashes, manure, straw, or waste material of any kind upon any street, alley, or public ground. 
Q.  Offensive Premises. Permitting any grocery store, shop, factory, warehouse, stable, barn, or other places to become nauseous or offensive. 
R.  Dangerous Agencies. Anything that is dangerous to human health or which renders the ground, the water, the air, or food a hazard or injury, to the public health. 
S.  Ice Boxes, Refrigerators, or Airtight Container. The keeping, leaving, or permitting to remain outside of any dwelling, building, or other structures or premises, in a place accessible to children, of any discarded ice boxes, refrigerators, or other container which has an air-tight door or lid, snap lock, or other locking device which may not be released from the inside, without first removing the door or lid, snap lock, or other locking device from the ice box, refrigerator, or container, is declared to be a nuisance and the person responsible for the violation shall be subject to a fine in an amount set by the city council and on file at the office of the finance officer, and the person shall also abate the nuisance according to Section 8.20.030 of this chapter. 
T.  Smokestacks and Smoke Nuisance. The construction, use, or maintenance of any smokestack or chimney which emits sparks, cinders, or dense smoke which is dangerous to the health, comfort, or property of persons, or the value of property. 
U.  Use of Sanitary Sewer. Permitting drainage water, blood, buttermilk, whey, by-products of milk, sewer pipe consuming acids, or any substance or material which interferes with the normal flow of sewage or prevents, blocks, or stops the flow of sewage. 
V.  Unconfined Refuse. The depositing, unloading, placing, storing, or otherwise piling of any dirt, straw, shavings, seeds, grain screenings, chaff, leaves, ashes, paper, or material of any kind upon property without covering the same in order to prevent it from being moved and blown about by wind upon property of another or upon any street, alley, or public property. 
W.  Dilapidated Buildings. A building or structure within the limits of the city which is so dilapidated, decayed, out of repair, unsafe, unsanitary, or utterly fails to provide the amenities essential to decent living such that it is unfit for human habitation and is likely to cause or is causing or aggravating sickness or disease so as to work an injury to the health, morals, safety, or general welfare of the community. 
(Prior code § 6-6-1) 
8.20.030 - Nuisances-Abatement. 
    The board of health shall give written notice to any person creating, permitting, or maintaining any nuisance to abate such nuisance forthwith, and if such person shall neglect or refuse to do so within a reasonable time after such notice, he or she shall be deemed guilty of violation of this chapter. The board of health shall cause to be removed or abated any such nuisance upon the expiration of a reasonable time after the serving of such notice, and the city may recover the expenses so incurred from the person maintaining such nuisance in a civil suit instituted for such purpose. 
(Prior code § 6-6-2) 
Chapter 8.24 - RAT ERADICATION 
Sections: 

8.24.010 - Definitions. 
    Terms used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise plainly requires, shall have the following meanings. 
    "Business building" means any structure, either public or private, that is adapted for occupancy for transaction of business, play, sale, or storage of goods, wares, or merchandise, or for the performance of work or labor, including but not being limited in this application, hotels, rooming houses, office buildings, public buildings, stores, theaters, markets, restaurants, grain elevators, and all buildings, sheds, barns, and other structures on premises used for business purposes. 
    "Occupant" means the individual or partnership who or the corporation that, has the use of or occupies any business building, or a part of or portion thereof, whether the actual owner, tenant, or subtenant. In the case of vacant buildings, or any vacant portion of a business building, the owner, agent, or other person having custody of the building, shall have the responsibilities of an "occupant" of the building. 
    "Owner" means the actual owner of the business building, either individual, partnership, or corporation, the person having custody of the building, and the person to whom any rental upon the building is to be paid. In the case of business buildings leased under agreement that the lessee is responsible for maintenance and repairs, the lessee will in such cases also be considered as the "owner" for the purpose of this chapter. 
    "Rat harborage" means any condition which provides shelter or protection for rats, thus favoring their multiplication and continuous existence in, under, or outside of a structure of any kind. 
    "Rat proofing" means a form of rat proofing to prevent the ingress into business buildings, from the exterior or from one business building to another. It consists essentially of the closing, with material impervious to rat gnawing, of all openings in the exterior wall, ground or first floors, basements and foundations, that may be reached by rats from the ground by climbing or by burrowing. 
(Prior code § 6-7-1) 
8.24.020 - Rat proofing buildings. 
    It is hereby provided and required that all business buildings in the city shall be rat proofed, freed of rats, and maintained in a rat proof and rat free condition, under the direction and supervision of the health officer. 
(Prior code § 6-7-2) 
8.24.030 - Notice to owner. 
    Upon receipt of written notice and/or order from the health officer, the owner of any building specified in the notice or order shall take immediate steps for rat proofing the buildings, and unless the work and improvements required for such rat proofing have been completed by the owner of the building in the time specified in the written notice or order, or within the time to which a written extension may have been granted by the health officer, then the owner shall be in violation of this chapter. 
(Prior code § 6-7-3) 
8.24.040 - Notice-Charge against owner. 
    Whenever the health officer notifies the occupant of a business that there is evidence of rat infestation of the building, the occupant shall immediately institute appropriate steps for freeing the building of rats within ten (10) days after receipt of such notice. If within ten (10) days the building is not free of rats, the city shall institute such action as is necessary and shall charge occupant for labor, material, and equipment necessary for the eradication measures carried out. 
(Prior code § 6-7-4) 
8.24.050 - Maintaining rat proofing condition. 
    The occupants of all rat proofed business buildings are required to maintain the premises in a rat proof condition and to repair all breaks and leaks that may occur in the rat proofing. 
(Prior code § 6-7-5) 
8.24.060 - Inspections. 
    The health officer is empowered to make unannounced inspections of both the interior and exterior of business buildings within the city as in their opinion may be necessary to determine whether there has been a full compliance with this chapter, and to require a full compliance with this chapter. If at any time of any inspection, the health officer finds evidence of rat infestation, and/or the existence of breaks or leaks in the rat proofing, or new openings through which rats may again enter the buildings, the city council shall serve upon the owner or occupant of the building a notice to abate the conditions so found. 
(Prior code § 6-7-6) 
8.24.070 - Installation of floors. 
    Whenever conditions inside or under business buildings provide such extensive harborage for rats that the health officer deems it necessary to eliminate such harborage, he or she may require the owner to install cement floors or basement or to replace wooden first floors or ground floors or require the owner to correct such other interior rat harborage as may be necessary in order to facilitate the eradication of rats in a reasonable length of time. 
(Prior code § 6-7-7) 
8.24.080 - Removal of rat proofing. 
    It is unlawful for the occupant, owner, contractor, public utility company, plumber, or any other person to remove the rat proofing from the same in a satisfactory condition; and, in like manner, it is unlawful for any such person to make any new openings that are not sealed or closed against the entrance of rats. 
(Prior code § 6-7-8) 
8.24.090 - Metal or plastic containers. 
    Everywhere within the city, all garbage or other refuse shall be placed and stored in covered metal or plastic containers, compartments, or rooms, unless kept in a rat proof building. 
(Prior code § 6-7-9) 
8.24.100 - Dumping of garbage and rubbish unlawful. 
    It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to place, leave, dump, or permit the accumulation of any garbage, rubbish, or trash in any building or upon any premises in the city so that the same shall or may provide food or harborage for rats. 
(Prior code § 6-7-10) 
8.24.110 - Storage of lumber and other material. 
    It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to permit to accumulate upon any premises whether improved or vacant, or upon any open lot or alley in the city, any lumber, boxes, barrels, bricks, stones, or any other materials that may be permitted to remain thereupon for any longer time than a temporary period reasonably required for the use of such materials in building or repairing of property, unless same shall be placed on open racks that are elevated not less than eighteen (18) inches above the ground, and evenly piled or stacked so that such material will not afford harborage for rats. 
(Prior code § 6-7-11) 
Chapter 8.28 - WEEDS 
Sections: 

8.28.010 - Duty of owner. 
    No owner, occupant, or other person in the charge of any lot, lots, tract, parcel, or any grounds in the city shall permit any grass or weeds to grow upon the property, or any grounds along any sidewalk adjoining the same, to a height exceeding three inches above such sidewalk or in any such manner as to impede, obstruct, or render inconvenient to travel upon the sidewalk; nor shall any owner, occupant, or person in charge of any lot or grounds in the city allow any weeds, grass, or other vegetation to grow thereon to a height exceeding ten (10) inches. 
(Prior code § 6-4-1) 
8.28.020 - Duty of chief of police. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police to see that all lots and grounds along the sidewalks are kept free from grass and weeds as hereinbefore provided and to notify all owners and occupants or persons responsible for such property of their duty to cut or remove the same. In case of default thereof by any such person within five days after being given written notice to cut or remove such weeds or grass, the chief of police of the city shall cause to be cut, mown, or removed such grass or weeds and shall cause the cost for removing and cutting same to be taxed and assessed against the lot, lots, tract, parcel, or grounds, and shall file with the county auditor of the county of Roberts and state of South Dakota, a statement of the costs incurred in cutting and removing such grass or weeds to be taxed against such property, and that the same shall become a lien upon such property immediately after the filing of such statement with the county auditor as herein provided. 
(Prior code § 6-4-2) 
Title 9 - PUBLIC PEACE, MORALS AND WELFARE 
Chapter 9.04 - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE AND DECENCY 
Sections: 

9.04.010 - Crowds obstructing streets. 
    It is unlawful for persons to gather in crowds or groups, or for any person to stand on any public street or sidewalk in such manner as to obstruct free passage thereon, or to annoy other persons passing along the same, and any police officer is authorized to disperse any crowd or group or to cause the removal of any person violating the provisions of this section, and to summarily arrest any person in case of refusal to obey any reasonable direction given by such officer for the purpose of clearing the way or preventing annoyance to any passerby on any public street or sidewalk. 
(Prior code § 8-2-1) 
9.04.020 - False emergency alarms prohibited. 
    No person shall knowingly make or give any false alarm of fire or other emergency, by calling or causing to be called the fire department, the police officers, or any authorized emergency vehicle. 
(Prior code § 8-1-3) 
9.04.030 - Open alcoholic beverages-Prohibitions. 
    No person shall take, carry, or have in his or her possession upon a street, alley, sidewalk, or public grounds of the city, or in any vehicle, any opened can, bottle, or other container in which there shall be any quantity of beer or other alcoholic beverage. 
(Prior code § 8-1-4) 
9.04.040 - Intentional use of aerosol propelled liquids, glue and gasoline as intoxicants. 
    It is illegal to intentionally use, sniff, or consume aerosol propelled liquids, glue, gasoline, or other substances as intoxicants by allowing those items to diminish the supply of oxygen going to the person's brain. 
(Prior code § 8-1-5) 
9.04.050 - Disorderly conduct. 
    Any person who intentionally causes serious public inconvenience, annoyance, or alarm to any other person, or creates a risk thereof by: 
A.  Engaging in fighting or in violent or threatening behavior; 
B.  Making unreasonable noise; 
C.  Disturbing any lawful assembly or meeting of persons without lawful authority; or 
D.  Obstructing vehicular or pedestrian traffic; is guilty of disorderly conduct. Disorderly conduct is punishable by a fine of up to two hundred dollars ($200.00) and/or jail sentence of up to thirty (30) days. 
(Ord. 546, 2002) 
9.04.060 - Fireworks and explosives. 
    It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to sell, keep for sale or offer for sale any firecrackers, torpedoes, rockets, or other fireworks of any description, or other such explosives or to discharge the same within one mile of the boundaries of the city. 
(Ord. 534, 2002: prior code § 8-5-2) 
9.04.070 - Loitering. 
A.
